<p><b>Beijing</b> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_postal_romanization" title="Chinese postal romanization">formerly</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Chinese" title="Romanization of Chinese">romanized</a> as <b>Peking</b><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>) is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> and the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population" title="List of cities proper by population">third most populous city proper</a>. It is also one of the world's most populous capital cities. The city, located in <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">northern China</a>, is governed as a <a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct-controlled municipality of the People's Republic of China">direct-controlled municipality</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the People's Republic of China">national government</a> with <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_divisions_of_Beijing" title="List of administrative divisions of Beijing">16 urban, suburban, and rural districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-figures_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-figures-9">[9]</a></sup> Beijing Municipality is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a> Province with the exception of neighboring <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a> Municipality to the southeast; together the three divisions form the <a href="/wiki/Jingjinji" title="Jingjinji">Jingjinji</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_of_China" title="Metropolitan regions of China">metropolitan region</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_capital_region" class="mw-redirect" title="National capital region">national capital region</a> of China.<sup id="cite_ref-basic_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basic-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beijing is the second largest Chinese city by <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China_by_urban_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in the People's Republic of China by urban population">urban population</a> after <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> and is the nation's <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Politics of the People's Republic of China">political</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">cultural</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Beijing" title="List of universities and colleges in Beijing">educational</a> center.<sup id="cite_ref-columbia_encyclopedia_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbia_encyclopedia-11">[11]</a></sup> It is home to the headquarters of most of <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_companies_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the largest companies of China">China's largest state-owned companies</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Beijing" title="Transport in Beijing">major hub</a> for the <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highways_of_Beijing" title="China National Highways of Beijing">national highway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Beijing" title="Expressways of Beijing">expressway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China#Current_network" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail transport in the People's Republic of China">railway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_China" title="High-speed rail in China">high-speed rail</a> networks. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing Capital International Airport</a> is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">second busiest in the world by passenger traffic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI_aero_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI_aero-12">[12]</a></sup> The city's <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">subway network</a> is among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">longest and busiest in the world</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Beijing" title="History of Beijing">city's history</a> dates back three <a href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">millennia</a>. As the last of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_capitals_of_China" title="Historical capitals of China">Four Great Ancient Capitals of China</a>, Beijing has been the political center of the country for much of the past eight centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The city is renowned for its opulent palaces, temples, parks, gardens, tombs, walls and gates,<sup id="cite_ref-world_book_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world_book-14">[14]</a></sup> and its art treasures and universities have made it a center of culture and art in China.<sup id="cite_ref-world_book_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world_book-14">[14]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i> notes that "few cities in the world have served for so long as the political headquarters and cultural centre of an area as immense as China."<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-15">[15]</a></sup> Beijing has <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_China" title="List of World Heritage Sites in China">seven</a> <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Summer_Palace" title="Summer Palace">Summer Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ming_Tombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Tombs">Ming Tombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhoukoudian" title="Zhoukoudian">Zhoukoudian</a>, as well as parts of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Wall">Great Wall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Beijing hosted the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> and was chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a>, which will make it the first city to ever host both events.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Etymology"></span><span id="Names"></span></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Beijing" title="Names of Beijing">Names of Beijing</a></div>
<p>Over the past 3,000 years, the city of Beijing has had <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Beijing" title="Names of Beijing">numerous other names</a>. The name <b>Beijing</b>, which means "Northern Capital" (from the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_characters" title="Chinese characters">Chinese characters</a> <span lang="zh">北</span> for <i>north</i> and <span lang="zh">京</span> for <i>capital</i>), was applied to the city in 1403 during the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a> to distinguish the city from <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> (the "Southern Capital").<sup id="cite_ref-minggov_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minggov-18">[18]</a></sup> The English spelling is based on the <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Chinese" title="Romanization of Chinese">romanization</a> of the two characters as they are pronounced in <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Standard Mandarin</a>. An older English spelling, <b>Peking</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/Postal_romanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Postal romanization">postal romanization</a> of the same two characters as they are pronounced in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Chinese dialects">Chinese dialects</a> spoken in the southern port towns first visited by European traders and missionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Those dialects preserve the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Chinese" title="Middle Chinese">Middle Chinese</a> pronunciation of <span lang="zh">京</span> as <i>kjaeng</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-BaxSag_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaxSag-20">[20]</a></sup> prior to a phonetic shift in the northern dialects to the modern pronunciation.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The single Chinese character abbreviation for Beijing is <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%BA%AC" class="extiw" title="wikt:京">京</a>, which appears on automobile license plates in the city. The official <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> <a href="/wiki/Standardization_Administration_of_China" title="Standardization Administration of China">abbreviation</a> for Beijing is "BJ".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Beijing" title="History of Beijing">History of Beijing</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The earliest traces of human habitation in the Beijing municipality were found in the caves of <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Bone_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragon Bone Hill">Dragon Bone Hill</a> near the village of <a href="/wiki/Zhoukoudian" title="Zhoukoudian">Zhoukoudian</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fangshan_District" title="Fangshan District">Fangshan District</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Peking_Man" title="Peking Man">Peking Man</a> lived. <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> fossils from the caves date to 230,000 to 250,000 years ago. <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> also lived there more recently, about 27,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Archaeologists have found <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">neolithic</a> settlements throughout the municipality, including in <a href="/wiki/Wangfujing" title="Wangfujing">Wangfujing</a>, located in downtown Beijing.</p>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Chinese_urban_planning" title="Ancient Chinese urban planning">walled city</a> in Beijing was <b><a href="/wiki/State_of_Ji" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Ji">Ji</a></b>, a city from the 11th to 7th century BC. Within modern Beijing, Ji was located south of the present <a href="/wiki/Beijing_West_Railway_Station" title="Beijing West Railway Station">Beijing West Railway Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-24">[24]</a></sup> This settlement was later conquered by the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Yan" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Yan">state of Yan</a> and made its capital under the name <b><a href="/wiki/Yanjing" title="Yanjing">Yanjing</a></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Imperial_China">Early Imperial China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early Imperial China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg/220px-Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg/330px-Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg/440px-Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3672" data-file-height="4896" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tianning_Temple_Pagoda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Pagoda_of_Tianning_Temple_(Beijing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pagoda of Tianning Temple (Beijing)">Tianning Pagoda</a>, built around 1120.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">First Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Qin%27s_wars_of_unification" title="Qin's wars of unification">unified China</a>, Beijing became a <a href="/wiki/Zhou_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhou (region)">prefectural capital</a> for the region.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-1">[1]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Kingdoms period">Three Kingdoms period</a>, it was held by <a href="/wiki/Gongsun_Zan" title="Gongsun Zan">Gongsun Zan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shao" title="Yuan Shao">Yuan Shao</a> before falling to <a href="/wiki/Cao_Cao" title="Cao Cao">Cao Cao</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Wei Kingdom</a>. The AD 3rd-century <a href="/wiki/Jin_Dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jin Dynasty (265–420)">Western Jin</a> demoted the town, placing the prefectural seat in neighboring Zhuozhou.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Kingdoms" title="Sixteen Kingdoms">Sixteen Kingdoms</a> period when northern China was conquered and divided by the <a href="/wiki/Five_Barbarians" title="Five Barbarians">Wu Hu</a>, Beijing, as <b><a href="/wiki/Jicheng_(Beijing)" title="Jicheng (Beijing)">Jicheng</a></b>, was briefly the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Xianbei" title="Xianbei">Xianbei</a> <a href="/wiki/Former_Yan" title="Former Yan">Former Yan</a> Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Rene_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rene-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>After China was reunified during the <a href="/wiki/Sui_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Sui Dynasty">Sui Dynasty</a>, Beijing, known as <b>Zhuojun</b>, became the northern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(China)" title="Grand Canal (China)">Grand Canal</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a>, Beijing as <b><a href="/wiki/Fanyang" class="mw-redirect" title="Fanyang">Fanyang</a></b>, served as a military frontier command center. During the <a href="/wiki/An-Shi_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="An-Shi Rebellion">An-Shi Rebellion</a> and again amidst the turmoil of the late Tang, local military commanders founded their own short-lived Yan Dynasties and called the city <b><a href="/wiki/Yanjing" title="Yanjing">Yanjing</a></b>, or the "Yan Capital." In 938, after the fall of the Tang, the <a href="/wiki/Later_Jin_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Jin (Five Dynasties)">Later Jin</a> ceded <a href="/wiki/Sixteen_Prefectures" title="Sixteen Prefectures">the entire northern frontier</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Khitan_people" title="Khitan people">Khitan</a> <a href="/wiki/Liao_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Liao Dynasty">Liao Dynasty</a>, which renamed the city <a href="/wiki/Liao_Nanjing" class="mw-redirect" title="Liao Nanjing">Nanjing</a>, or the "Southern Capital", one of four secondary capitals to complement its "Supreme Capital", Shangjing (modern <a href="/wiki/Baarin_Left_Banner" class="mw-redirect" title="Baarin Left Banner">Baarin Left Banner</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>). Some of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_pagodas_in_Beijing" title="List of pagodas in Beijing">oldest surviving structures in Beijing</a> date to the Liao period, including the <a href="/wiki/Pagoda_of_Tianning_Temple_(Beijing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pagoda of Tianning Temple (Beijing)">Tianning Pagoda</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg/220px-%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg/330px-%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg/440px-%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2882" data-file-height="1444" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E9%A2%90%E5%92%8C%E5%9B%AD%E4%BD%9B%E9%A6%99%E9%98%81.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Longevity_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Longevity Hill">Longevity Hill</a> in Beijing where <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> wrote his poem.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Liao fell to the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jurchen Jin dynasty</a> in 1122, which gave the city to the <a href="/wiki/Song_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Song Dynasty">Song Dynasty</a> and then retook it in 1125 during its <a href="/wiki/Jin_campaigns_against_the_Song_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Jin campaigns against the Song Dynasty">conquest of northern China</a>. In 1153, the Jurchen Jin made Beijing their "Central Capital", called <b>Zhongdu</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-1">[1]</a></sup> The city was besieged by <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>'s invading <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongolian army</a> in 1213 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zhongdu" title="Battle of Zhongdu">razed to the ground</a> two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-economist_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-27">[27]</a></sup> Two generations later, <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> ordered the construction of <b><a href="/wiki/Khanbaliq" title="Khanbaliq">Dadu</a></b> (or Daidu to the Mongols, commonly known as Khanbaliq), a new capital for his <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> to be located adjacent to the Jurchen Jin ruins. The construction took from 1264 to 1293,<sup id="cite_ref-hist_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-economist_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> but greatly enhanced the status of a city on the northern fringe of <a href="/wiki/China_proper" title="China proper">China proper</a>. The city was centered on the <a href="/wiki/Drum_Tower_and_Bell_Tower_of_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Drum Tower and Bell Tower of Beijing">Drum Tower</a> slightly to the north of modern Beijing and stretched from the present-day <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an_Avenue" title="Chang'an Avenue">Chang'an Avenue</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Line_10,_Beijing_Subway" title="Line 10, Beijing Subway">Line 10 subway</a>. Remnants of the Yuan <a href="/wiki/Rammed_earth" title="Rammed earth">rammed earth</a> wall still stand and are known as the Tucheng.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ming_dynasty">Ming dynasty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ming dynasty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BeijingWatchTower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BeijingWatchTower.jpg/220px-BeijingWatchTower.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BeijingWatchTower.jpg/330px-BeijingWatchTower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/BeijingWatchTower.jpg/440px-BeijingWatchTower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="573" data-file-height="478" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BeijingWatchTower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the corner towers of the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1368, soon after declaring the new <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu era</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Turban_rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Turban rebellion">rebel</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Yuanzhang" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhu Yuanzhang">Zhu Yuanzhang</a> sent an army to Khanbaliq and conquered it.<sup id="cite_ref-patbu_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patbu-30">[30]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Yuan_dynasty" title="Northern Yuan dynasty">Yuan</a> continued to occupy <a href="/wiki/Xanadu,_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Xanadu, China">Shangdu</a> and Mongolia, however, a new town was established to supply the military garrisons in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This was called <b>Beiping</b><sup id="cite_ref-peking_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peking-32">[32]</a></sup> and under the Hongwu Emperor's feudal policies it was given to <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Di" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhu Di">Zhu Di</a>, one of his sons, who was created "<a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Yan" title="Prince of Yan">Prince of Yan</a>".</p>
<p>The early death of <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Yuanzhang" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhu Yuanzhang">Zhu Yuanzhang</a>'s heir led to a <a href="/wiki/Jingnan_Campaign" title="Jingnan Campaign">succession struggle</a> on his death, one that ended with the victory of <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Di" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhu Di">Zhu Di</a> and the declaration of the new <a href="/wiki/Yongle_Emperor" title="Yongle Emperor">Yongle era</a>. Since his harsh treatment of the Ming capital Yingtian (Nanjing) alienated many there, he established his fief as a new co-capital. The city of <a href="/wiki/Beiping" title="Beiping">Beiping</a> became <a href="/wiki/Shuntian_Prefecture" title="Shuntian Prefecture">Shuntian</a><sup id="cite_ref-WDL1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL1-33">[33]</a></sup> in 1403.<sup id="cite_ref-minggov_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minggov-18">[18]</a></sup> The construction of the new imperial residence, the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, took from 1406 to 1420;<sup id="cite_ref-economist_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-27">[27]</a></sup> this period was also responsible for several other of the modern city's major attractions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tian%27anmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tian'anmen">Tian'anmen</a> (although the <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square" title="Tiananmen Square">square facing it</a> was not cleared until 1651<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>). On 28 October 1420, the city was officially designated the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a> in the same year that the Forbidden City was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-Hymes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hymes-36">[36]</a></sup> Beijing became the empire's primary capital (<b>Jingshi</b>) and Yingtian – or called <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> – became the co-capital. (A 1425 order by Zhu Di's son, the <a href="/wiki/Hongxi_Emperor" title="Hongxi Emperor">Hongxi Emperor</a>, to return the capital to Nanjing was never carried out: he died, probably of a heart attack, the next month. He was buried, like almost every Ming emperor to follow him, in an <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty_Tombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty Tombs">elaborate necropolis</a> to Beijing's north.)</p>
<p>By the 15th century, Beijing had essentially taken its current shape. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_city_fortifications" title="Beijing city fortifications">Ming city wall</a> continued to serve until modern times, when it was pulled down and the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="2nd Ring Road">2nd Ring Road</a> was built in its place.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It is generally believed that Beijing was the largest city in the world for most of the 15th, 16th, 17th, and 18th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_China" title="Christianity in China">first known church</a> was constructed by <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_China_Missions" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuit China Missions">Catholics</a> in 1652 at the former site of <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Ricci" title="Matteo Ricci">Matteo Ricci</a>'s chapel; the modern <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Immaculate_Conception_in_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception in Beijing">Nantang Cathedral</a> was later built upon the same site.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The capture of Beijing by <a href="/wiki/Li_Zicheng" title="Li Zicheng">Li Zicheng</a>'s peasant army in 1644 ended the dynasty, but he and his <a href="/wiki/Shun_dynasty" title="Shun dynasty">Shun court</a> abandoned the city without a fight when the <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a> army of Prince <a href="/wiki/Dorgon" title="Dorgon">Dorgon</a> arrived 40 days later.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qing_dynasty">Qing dynasty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Qing dynasty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hata-men_Gate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hata-men_Gate.jpg/220px-Hata-men_Gate.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hata-men_Gate.jpg/330px-Hata-men_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hata-men_Gate.jpg/440px-Hata-men_Gate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1583" data-file-height="1113" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hata-men_Gate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chongwenmen" title="Chongwenmen">Chongwenmen</a>, a gate to the inner walled city, c. 1906</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dorgon" title="Dorgon">Dorgon</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> as a direct successor of the Ming (delegitimizing <a href="/wiki/Li_Zicheng" title="Li Zicheng">Li Zicheng</a> and his followers)<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_ming_qing_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica_ming_qing-40">[40]</a></sup> and Beijing became China's sole capital.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The Qing emperors made some modifications to the Imperial residence but, in large part, the Ming buildings and the general layout remained unchanged. Facilities for Manchu worship were introduced, but the Qing also continued the traditional state rituals. Signage was bilingual or Chinese. This early Qing Beijing later formed the setting for the <a href="/wiki/Four_Great_Classical_Novels" title="Four Great Classical Novels">Chinese novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Dream_of_the_Red_Chamber" title="Dream of the Red Chamber">Dream of the Red Chamber</a></i>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Opium_War" title="Second Opium War">Second Opium War</a>, Anglo-French forces captured the city, looting and burning the <a href="/wiki/Old_Summer_Palace" title="Old Summer Palace">Old Summer Palace</a> in 1860. Under the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Peking" title="Convention of Peking">Convention of Peking</a> ending that war, Western powers for the first time secured the right to establish <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Legation_Quarter" title="Beijing Legation Quarter">permanent diplomatic presences</a> within the city. In 1900, the attempt by the "<a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxers</a>" to eradicate this presence, as well as Chinese Christian converts, led to Beijing's reoccupation by <a href="/wiki/Eight-Nation_Alliance" title="Eight-Nation Alliance">foreign powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> During the fighting, several important structures were destroyed, including the <a href="/wiki/Hanlin_Academy" title="Hanlin Academy">Hanlin Academy</a> and the (new) <a href="/wiki/Summer_Palace" title="Summer Palace">Summer Palace</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China">Republic of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Republic of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:712px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/1937_Peking%2C_China_VP8.webm/712px--1937_Peking%2C_China_VP8.webm.jpg&quot; type=&quot;video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Ogg video (360P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;Ogg 360P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;360p.ogv&quot; data-width=&quot;534&quot; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1937_Peking,_China_VP8.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beijing filmed in 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The fomenters of the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> of 1911 sought to replace Qing rule with a republic and leaders like <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> originally intended to return the capital to Nanjing. After the Qing general <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a> forced the abdication of the last Qing emperor and ensured the success of the revolution, the revolutionaries accepted him as president of the new <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a>. Yuan maintained his capital at Beijing and quickly consolidated power, declaring himself emperor in 1915. His death less than a year later<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> left China under the control of the warlords commanding the regional armies. Following the success of the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Nationalists</a>' <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition_(1926%E2%80%931927)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Expedition (1926–1927)">Northern Expedition</a>, the capital was formally removed to Nanjing in 1928. On 28 June the same year, Beijing's name was returned to Beiping (written at the time as "Peiping").<sup id="cite_ref-columbia_encyclopedia_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbia_encyclopedia-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-columbia_encyclopedia_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbia_encyclopedia-11">[11]</a></sup> Beiping fell to Japan on 29 July 1937<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and was made the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_Republic_of_China_(1937%E2%80%931940)" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional Government of the Republic of China (1937–1940)">Provisional Government of the Republic of China</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> that ruled the ethnic-Chinese portions of Japanese-occupied <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">northern China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> This government was later merged into the larger <a href="/wiki/Reorganized_National_Government_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Reorganized National Government of China">Wang Jingwei government</a> based in Nanjing.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People.27s_Republic_of_China">People's Republic of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: People's Republic of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PRCFounding.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/PRCFounding.jpg/220px-PRCFounding.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/PRCFounding.jpg/330px-PRCFounding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/PRCFounding.jpg/440px-PRCFounding.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PRCFounding.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> proclaiming the establishment of the People's Republic of China in 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the final phases of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> seized control of the city peacefully on 31 January 1949 in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Pingjin_Campaign" title="Pingjin Campaign">Pingjin Campaign</a>. On 1 October that year, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> announced the creation of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> from atop <a href="/wiki/Tian%27anmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tian'anmen">Tian'anmen</a>. He restored the name of the city, as the new capital, to Beijing,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> a decision that had been reached by the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Political_Consultative_Conference" title="Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference">Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference</a> just a few days earlier.</p>
<p>In the 1950s, the city began to expand beyond the old walled city and its surrounding neighborhoods, with heavy industries in <a href="/wiki/Shijingshan_District" title="Shijingshan District">the west</a> and residential neighborhoods in <a href="/wiki/Hepingli_Subdistrict,_Beijing" title="Hepingli Subdistrict, Beijing">the north</a>. Many areas of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_city_fortifications" title="Beijing city fortifications">Beijing city wall</a> were torn down in the 1960s to make way for the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">Beijing Subway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="2nd Ring Road">2nd Ring Road</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg/220px-Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg/330px-Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg/440px-Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="508" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A scene from the opening ceremonies of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Summer Olympic Games">2008 Summer Olympic Games</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> from 1966 to 1976, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Guard_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Guard (China)">Red Guard</a> movement began in Beijing and the city's government fell victim to one of the first purges. By the fall of 1966, all city schools were shut down and over a million Red Guards from across the country gathered in Beijing for eight rallies in Tian'anmen Square with Mao.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In April 1976, a large public gathering of Beijing residents against the <a href="/wiki/Gang_of_Four" title="Gang of Four">Gang of Four</a> and the Cultural Revolution in Tiananmen Square <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Incident" title="Tiananmen Incident">was forcefully suppressed</a>. In October 1976, the Gang was arrested in <a href="/wiki/Zhongnanhai" title="Zhongnanhai">Zhongnanhai</a> and the Cultural Revolution came to an end. In December 1978, the <a href="/wiki/Third_Plenary_Session_of_the_11th_CPC_Central_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Plenary Session of the 11th CPC Central Committee">Third Plenum of the 11th Party Congress</a> in Beijing under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> reversed the verdicts against victims of the Cultural Revolution and instituted the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">"policy of reform and opening up."</a></p>
<p>Since the early 1980s, the urban area of Beijing has expanded greatly with the completion of the 2nd Ring Road in 1981 and the subsequent addition of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Ring_Road_(Beijing)" title="3rd Ring Road (Beijing)">3rd</a>, <a href="/wiki/4th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="4th Ring Road">4th</a>, <a href="/wiki/5th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="5th Ring Road">5th</a> and <a href="/wiki/6th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="6th Ring Road">6th Ring Roads</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> According to one 2005 newspaper report, the size of newly developed Beijing was one-and-a-half times larger than before.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wangfujing" title="Wangfujing">Wangfujing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xidan" title="Xidan">Xidan</a> have developed into flourishing shopping districts,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Zhongguancun" title="Zhongguancun">Zhongguancun</a> has become a major center of electronics in China.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In recent years, the expansion of Beijing has also brought to the forefront some problems of urbanization, such as <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">heavy traffic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">poor air quality</a>, the loss of historic neighborhoods, and a significant influx of migrant workers from less-developed <a href="/wiki/Rural_area" title="Rural area">rural areas</a> of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Beijing has also been the location of many significant events in recent Chinese history, principally the <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square_protests_of_1989" title="Tiananmen Square protests of 1989">Tiananmen Square protests of 1989</a><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-56">[56]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>. This city was awarded to host the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015 World Championships in Athletics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Beijing" title="Geography of Beijing">Geography of Beijing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg/170px-Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg/255px-Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg/340px-Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Large_Beijing_Landsat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Landsat_7" title="Landsat 7">Landsat 7</a> Satellite image of Beijing Municipality with the surrounding mountains in dark brown</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beijing is situated at the northern tip of the roughly triangular <a href="/wiki/North_China_Plain" title="North China Plain">North China Plain</a>, which opens to the south and east of the city. Mountains to the north, northwest and west shield the city and northern China's agricultural heartland from the encroaching desert steppes. The northwestern part of the municipality, especially <a href="/wiki/Yanqing_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Yanqing County">Yanqing County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huairou_District" title="Huairou District">Huairou District</a>, are dominated by the Jundu Mountains, while the western part is framed by <i>Xishan</i> or the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hills" title="Western Hills">Western Hills</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a> across the northern part of Beijing Municipality was built on the rugged topography to defend against nomadic incursions from the steppes. Mount Dongling, in the Western Hills and on the border with <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a>, is the municipality's highest point, with an altitude of 2,303 metres (7,556&#160;ft).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GreatWall6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GreatWall6.jpg/220px-GreatWall6.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GreatWall6.jpg/330px-GreatWall6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GreatWall6.jpg/440px-GreatWall6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1474" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GreatWall6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a> in the mountains north of the city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major rivers flowing through the municipality, including the <a href="/wiki/Chaobai_River" title="Chaobai River">Chaobai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yongding_River" title="Yongding River">Yongding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juma_River_(China)" title="Juma River (China)">Juma</a>, are all tributaries in the <a href="/wiki/Hai_River" title="Hai River">Hai River</a> system, and flow in a southeasterly direction. The Miyun Reservoir, on the upper reaches of the Chaobai River, is the largest reservoir within the municipality. Beijing is also the northern terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Canal of China">Grand Canal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, which was built over 1,400 years ago as a transportation route, and the <a href="/wiki/South%E2%80%93North_Water_Transfer_Project" title="South–North Water Transfer Project">South–North Water Transfer Project</a>, constructed in the past decade to bring water from the <a href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> basin.</p>
<p>The urban area of Beijing, on the plains in the south-central of the municipality with elevation of 40&#160;to 60 metres (130–200 feet), occupies a relatively small but expanding portion of the municipality's area. The city spreads out in concentric <a href="/wiki/Ring_Roads_of_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring Roads of Beijing">ring roads</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Ring_Road_(Beijing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Ring Road (Beijing)">Second Ring Road</a> traces the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_city_wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing city wall">old city walls</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sixth_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Sixth Ring Road">Sixth Ring Road</a> connects satellite towns in the surrounding suburbs. <a href="/wiki/Tian%27anmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tian'anmen">Tian'anmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tian%27anmen_Square" class="mw-redirect" title="Tian'anmen Square">Tian'anmen Square</a> are at the center of Beijing, directly to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, the former residence of the emperors of China. To the west of Tian'anmen is <a href="/wiki/Zhongnanhai" title="Zhongnanhai">Zhongnanhai</a>, the residence of China's current leaders. <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an_Avenue" title="Chang'an Avenue">Chang'an Avenue</a>, which cuts between Tiananmen and the Square, forms the city's main east-west axis.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing has a monsoon-influenced <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dwa</i>), characterized by higher humidity in the summers due to the East Asian <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>, and colder, windier, drier winters that reflect the influence of the vast <a href="/wiki/Siberian_anticyclone" class="mw-redirect" title="Siberian anticyclone">Siberian anticyclone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-people.27s_daily_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people.27s_daily-58">[58]</a></sup> Spring can bear witness to sandstorms blowing in from the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian-Manchurian_grassland" title="Mongolian-Manchurian grassland">Mongolian steppe</a>, accompanied by rapidly warming, but generally dry, conditions. Autumn, like spring, is a season of transition and minimal precipitation. The monthly daily average temperature in January is −3.7&#160;°C (25.3&#160;°F), while in July it is 26.2&#160;°C (79.2&#160;°F). <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> averages around 570&#160;mm (22&#160;in) annually, with close to three-fourths of that total falling from June to August. With monthly percent possible sunshine ranging from 47% in July to 65% in January and February, the city receives 2,671 hours of bright sunshine annually. Extremes since 1951 have ranged from −27.4&#160;°C (−17.3&#160;°F) on 22 February 1966 to 41.9&#160;°C (107.4&#160;°F) on 24 July 1999 (unofficial record of 42.6&#160;°C (108.7&#160;°F) was set on 15 June 1942).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mherrera_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mherrera-60">[60]</a></sup></p>

</tr>

</tr>

<p><br /></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing has a long history of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_problems" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental problems">environmental problems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2009 Beijing's urban extent quadrupled, which not only strongly increased the extent of anthropogenic emissions, but also changed the meteorological situation fundamentally, even if <a href="/wiki/Exhaust_gas" title="Exhaust gas">emissions</a> of human society are not included. For example, surface <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">albedo</a>, wind speed and <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a> near the surface were decreased, whereas ground and near-surface <a href="/wiki/Air_temperature" class="mw-redirect" title="Air temperature">air temperatures</a>, vertical air dilution and <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> levels were increased.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Because of the combined factors of urbanization and pollution caused by burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a>, Beijing is often affected by serious environmental problems, which lead to <a href="/wiki/Health" title="Health">health</a> issues of many inhabitants. In 2013 heavy <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a> struck Beijing and most parts of northern China, in total 600 million people. After this "pollution shock" <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> became an important economic and social concern in China. After that the government of Beijing announced measures to reduce air pollution, for example by lowering the share of coal from 24% in 2012 to 10% in 2017, while the national government ordered heavily polluting vehicles to be removed from 2015 to 2017 and increased its efforts to transition the energy system to clean sources.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_quality">Air quality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Air quality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Joint research between American and Chinese researchers in 2006 concluded that much of the city's pollution comes from surrounding cities and provinces. On average 35–60% of the <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> can be traced to sources outside the city. <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a> Province and <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a> Municipality have a "significant influence on Beijing's air quality",<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> partly due to the prevailing south/southeasterly flow during the summer and the mountains to the north and northwest.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png/350px-Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png" width="350" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png/525px-Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png/700px-Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_smog_comparison_August_2005.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Heavy air pollution has resulted in widespread smog. These photographs, taken in August 2005, show the variations in Beijing's air quality.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> and to fulfill promises to clean up the city's air, nearly 17&#160;billion USD was spent.<sup id="cite_ref-sundance_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundance-68">[68]</a></sup> Beijing implemented a number of air improvement schemes for the duration of the Games, including halting work at all construction sites, closing many factories in Beijing permanently, temporarily shutting industry in neighboring regions, closing some gas stations,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Road_space_rationing_in_Beijing" title="Road space rationing in Beijing">cutting motor traffic by half by limiting drivers to odd or even days (based on their license plate numbers)</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> reducing bus and subway fares, opening new subway lines, and banning high-emission vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-octpoll_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-octpoll-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-polluteban_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polluteban-72">[72]</a></sup> The city further assembled 3,800 <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>-powered buses, one of the largest fleets in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-sundance_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundance-68">[68]</a></sup> Beijing became the first city in China to require the Chinese equivalent to the Euro 4 <a href="/wiki/Emission_standard" title="Emission standard">emission standard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Coal burning accounts for about 40% of the <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">PM 2.5</a> in Beijing and is also the chief source of nitrogen and sulfur dioxide.<sup id="cite_ref-MotherJones_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotherJones-74">[74]</a></sup> Since 2012, the city has been converting coal-fired <a href="/wiki/List_of_major_power_stations_in_Beijing" title="List of major power stations in Beijing">power stations</a> to burn natural gas<sup id="cite_ref-CNDaily20120308_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNDaily20120308-75">[75]</a></sup> and aims to cap annual coal consumption at 20 million tons. In 2011, the city burned 26.3 million tons of coal, 73% of which for heating and power generation and the remainder for industry.<sup id="cite_ref-CNDaily20120308_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNDaily20120308-75">[75]</a></sup> Much of the city's air pollutants are emitted by neighboring regions.<sup id="cite_ref-MotherJones_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotherJones-74">[74]</a></sup> Coal consumption in neighboring Tianjin is expected to increase from 48 to 63 million tons from 2011 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMP20130205_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMP20130205-76">[76]</a></sup> Hebei Province burned over 300 million tons of coal in 2011, more than all of Germany, of which only 30% were used for power generation and a considerable portion for steel and cement making.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Power plants in the coal-mining regions of Shanxi, Inner Mongolia and Shaanxi, where coal consumption has tripled since 2000, and Shandong also contribute to air pollution in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-MotherJones_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MotherJones-74">[74]</a></sup> Shandong, Shanxi, Hebei and Inner Mongolia, respectively rank from first to fourth, among Chinese provinces by coal consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMP20130205_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMP20130205-76">[76]</a></sup> There were four major coal-fired power plants in the city to provide electricity as well as heating during the winter. The first one (Gaojing Thermal Power Plant) was shut down in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Another two were shut in March 2015. The last one (Huaneng Thermal Power Plant) would be shut in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily-78">[78]</a></sup> Between 2013 and 2017, the city planned to reduce 13 million tons of coal consumption and cap coal consumption to 15 million tons in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaDaily_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaDaily-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government regularly uses <a href="/wiki/Cloud-seeding" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloud-seeding">cloud-seeding</a> measures to increase the likelihood of rain showers in the region to clear the air prior to large events<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> as well as to combat drought conditions in the area.</p>
<p>Beijing air quality is often poor, especially in winter. In mid-January 2013, Beijing's air quality was measured on top of <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Beijing" title="Embassy of the United States, Beijing">the city's American embassy</a> at a PM2.5 density of 755 micrograms per cubic meter, which went off the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency's air quality index. It was widely reported, originally through a Twitter account, that the category was "crazy bad". This was later changed to "beyond index".<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 and 9 December 2015 Beijing had its first <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a> alert which shut down a majority of the industry and other commercial businesses in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Later in the month another smog "red alert" was issued.<sup id="cite_ref-abc-2nd-red_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-2nd-red-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Readings">Readings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Readings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Due to Beijing's high-level of air pollution, there are various readings by different sources on the subject. Daily pollution readings at 27 monitoring stations around the city are reported on the website of the Beijing Environmental Protection Bureau (BJEPB).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The American Embassy of Beijing also reports hourly <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">fine particulate (PM2.5)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> levels on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-Demick_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demick-85">[85]</a></sup> Since the BJEPB and US Embassy measure different pollutants according to different criteria, the pollution levels and the impact to human health reported by the BJEPB are often lower than that reported by the US Embassy.<sup id="cite_ref-Demick_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demick-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:902px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg/900px-2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg.png" width="900" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg/1350px-2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg/1800px-2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="926" data-file-height="264" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2015_Air_pollution_in_Beijing.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2015 Air pollution in Beijing as measured by <a href="/wiki/Air_quality_index#Mainland_China" title="Air quality index">Air Quality Index (AQI)</a>
<div class="columns-2" style="background-color: transparent; width: 100%">
<div class="column">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #7e0023; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Severely Polluted</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #9900ac; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Heavily Polluted</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Moderately Polluted</div>
</div>
<div class="column">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff7e00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Lightly Polluted</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Good</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00e400; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Excellent</div>
</div>
<div style="clear: both"></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dust_storms">Dust storms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dust storms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Dust from the erosion of deserts in northern and northwestern China results in seasonal <a href="/wiki/Dust_storm" title="Dust storm">dust storms</a> that plague the city; the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Weather_Modification_Office" title="Beijing Weather Modification Office">Beijing Weather Modification Office</a> sometimes artificially induces rainfall to fight such storms and mitigate their effects.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In the first four months of 2006 alone, there were no fewer than eight such storms.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In April 2002, one dust storm alone dumped nearly 50,000&#160;tons of dust onto the city before moving on to Japan and Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Beijing" title="Politics of Beijing">Politics of Beijing</a></div>
<p>Municipal government is regulated by the local <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party of China</a> (CPC), led by the Beijing <a href="/wiki/CPC_Secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="CPC Secretary">CPC Secretary</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">北京市委书记</span>). The local CPC issues administrative orders, collects taxes, manages the economy, and directs a standing committee of the Municipal People's Congress in making policy decisions and overseeing the local government.</p>
<p>Government officials include the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Beijing">mayor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">市长</span>) and vice-mayor. Numerous bureaus focus on law, public security, and other affairs. Additionally, as the capital of China, Beijing houses all of the important national governmental and political institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Congress" title="National People's Congress">National People's Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_government_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica_government-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_divisions_of_Beijing" title="List of administrative divisions of Beijing">List of administrative divisions of Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_township-level_divisions_of_Beijing" title="List of township-level divisions of Beijing">List of township-level divisions of Beijing</a></div>
<p>Beijing Municipality currently comprises 16 administrative <a href="/wiki/County-level_division" class="mw-redirect" title="County-level division">county-level subdivisions</a> including 16 urban, suburban, and rural <a href="/wiki/District_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="District of China">districts</a>. On 1 July 2010, <a href="/wiki/Chongwen_District" title="Chongwen District">Chongwen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xuanwu_District,_Beijing" title="Xuanwu District, Beijing">Xuanwu</a> were merged into Dongcheng and Xicheng, respectively. On 13 November 2015 <a href="/wiki/Miyun_District" title="Miyun District">Miyun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yanqing_District" title="Yanqing District">Yanqing</a> were upgraded to districts.</p>

<a href="/wiki/Shichahai" title="Shichahai">Shichahai</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Xicheng_District" title="Xicheng District">Xicheng District</a>, is traditionally considered one of Beijing's most beautiful and charming scenic areas.</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Towns">Towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_township-level_divisions_of_Beijing" title="List of township-level divisions of Beijing">List of township-level divisions of Beijing</a></div>
<p>Beijing's 16 county-level divisions (districts) are further subdivided into 273 lower third-level administrative units at the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China#Township_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of the People's Republic of China">township level</a>: 119 <a href="/wiki/Town_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Town of China">towns</a>, 24 <a href="/wiki/Townships_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Townships of the People's Republic of China">townships</a>, 5 <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_township" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic township">ethnic townships</a> and 125 <a href="/wiki/Subdistricts_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdistricts of China">subdistricts</a>. Towns within Beijing Municipality but outside the urban area include (but are not limited to):</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Changping_District" title="Changping District">Changping</a> <span lang="zh">昌平</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huairou" class="mw-redirect" title="Huairou">Huairou</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">怀柔</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miyun" class="mw-redirect" title="Miyun">Miyun</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">密云</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liangxiang,_Beijing" title="Liangxiang, Beijing">Liangxiang</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">良乡</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liulimiao" title="Liulimiao">Liulimiao</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">琉璃庙</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tongzhou_District,_Beijing" title="Tongzhou District, Beijing">Tongzhou</a> <span lang="zh">通州</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yizhuang,_Beijing" title="Yizhuang, Beijing">Yizhuang</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">亦庄</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tiantongyuan" title="Tiantongyuan">Tiantongyuan</a> <span lang="zh">天通苑</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beiyuan,_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Beiyuan, Beijing">Beiyuan</a> <span lang="zh">北苑</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xiaotangshan" title="Xiaotangshan">Xiaotangshan</a> <span lang="zh-Hans">小汤山</span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>Several place names in Beijing end with <i>mén</i> (<span lang="zh-Hans">门</span>), meaning "gate", as they were the locations of gates in the former <a href="/wiki/Beijing_city_fortifications" title="Beijing city fortifications">Beijing city wall</a>. Other place names end in <i>cūn</i> (<span lang="zh">村</span>), meaning "village", as they were originally villages outside the city wall.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighbourhoods">Neighbourhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Neighbourhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niujie_Mosque_-_CIMG3671.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Niujie_Mosque" title="Niujie Mosque">Niujie Mosque</a> is an important historical attraction</div>

</div>
