<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary_and_procuracy">Judiciary and procuracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Judiciary and procuracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial system of the People's Republic of China">judicial system</a> in Beijing consists of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_People%27s_Court" title="Supreme People's Court">Supreme People's Court</a>, the highest court in the country, the Beijing Municipal High People's Court, the <a href="/wiki/High_people%27s_court" title="High people's court">high people's court</a> of the municipality, three <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_people%27s_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="Intermediate people's courts">intermediate people's courts</a>, one intermediate <a href="/wiki/Railway_Transport_Court_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway Transport Court (People's Republic of China)">railway transport court</a>, 14 <a href="/wiki/Basic_people%27s_court" title="Basic people's court">basic people's court</a> (one for each of the municipality's districts and counties), and one basic railway transport court. The Beijing No. 1 Intermediate People's Court in Shijingshan oversees the basic courts of Haidian, Shijingshan, Mentougou, Changping and Yanqing.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuacourts_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuacourts-96">[94]</a></sup> The Beijing No. 2 Intermediate People's Court in Fengtai oversees the basic courts of Dongcheng, Xicheng, Fengtai, Fangshan and Daxing.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuacourts_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuacourts-96">[94]</a></sup> The Beijing No. 3 Intermediate People's Court in Laiguangying, is the newest of the three intermediate people's courts and opened on 21 August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuacourts_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuacourts-96">[94]</a></sup> It oversees the district courts of Chaoyang, Tongzhou, Shunyi, Huairou, Pinggu and Miyun.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhuacourts_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhuacourts-96">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BJcourts_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BJcourts-97">[95]</a></sup> Each court in Beijing has a corresponding <a href="/wiki/Supreme_People%27s_Procuratorate" title="Supreme People's Procuratorate">people's procuratorate</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diplomatic_missions">Diplomatic missions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Diplomatic missions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_China" title="List of diplomatic missions in China">List of diplomatic missions in China</a></div>
<p>About <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China#Embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of diplomatic missions in the People's Republic of China">163 countries have embassies in Beijing</a>, which are concentrated in Jiangguomenwai, <a href="/wiki/Sanlitun" title="Sanlitun">Sanlitun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liangmaqiao" class="mw-redirect" title="Liangmaqiao">Liangmaqiao</a> in Chaoyang District.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Beijing" title="Economy of Beijing">Economy of Beijing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wangfujing_street,_Beijing.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG/220px-Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG/330px-Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG/440px-Wangfujing_street%2C_Beijing.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wangfujing_street,_Beijing.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wangfujing" title="Wangfujing">Wangfujing</a> Street is one of the oldest and busiest shopping streets in Beijing with nearly 100,000 visitors daily (August 2008). The sale of consumer goods both retail and wholesale accounted for about ⅛ of Beijing's economic output in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beijing's economy ranks among the most developed and prosperous in China. In 2013, the municipality's <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal gross domestic product (GDP)</a> was <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" title="Chinese yuan">CN￥</a>1.95 trillion (US$314 billion), about 3.43% of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_GDP_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical GDP of the People's Republic of China">country's total output</a>, and ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_administrative_divisions_by_GDP" title="List of Chinese administrative divisions by GDP">13th</a> among <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_China" title="Administrative divisions of China">province-level administrative units</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gdp2013_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdp2013-99">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Per capita GDP">Per capita GDP</a>, at CN￥93,213 (US$15,051) in nominal terms and <a href="/wiki/Geary%E2%80%93Khamis_dollar" title="Geary–Khamis dollar">Int$</a>21,948 at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>, was 2.2 times the national average and ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_administrative_divisions_by_GDP_per_capita" title="List of Chinese administrative divisions by GDP per capita">second</a> among province-level administrative units.<sup id="cite_ref-gdppc2013_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdppc2013-100">[98]</a></sup> The economy tripled in size from 2004 to 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-JLL_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JLL-101">[99]</a></sup> and grew at an annual rate of 7.7% in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the concentration of <a href="/wiki/List_of_State-owned_enterprises_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of State-owned enterprises in China">state owned enterprises</a> in the national capital, Beijing in 2013 had more <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> Company headquarters than any other city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-JLL_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JLL-101">[99]</a></sup> Beijing ranks 9th in the world in the International Financial Centres Development Index published by the <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua News Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Mercantile_Exchange" title="Chicago Mercantile Exchange">Chicago Mercantile Exchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_%26_Company" title="Dow Jones &amp; Company">Dow Jones &amp; Company</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> and 23rd in the world in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Z/Yen" title="Z/Yen">Z/Yen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Financial_Centre" title="Qatar Financial Centre">Qatar Financial Centre</a> Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-GFCI_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI-103">[101]</a></sup> The city also ranked No. 1 in the number of billionaire more than Moscow, New York and Hong Kong. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> rated Beijing's overall economic influence as No. 1 in China.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sector_composition">Sector composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sector composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg/220px-Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg/330px-Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg/440px-Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Taikoo_Li_Sanlitun" title="Taikoo Li Sanlitun">Taikoo Li Sanlitun</a> shopping arcade is a popular destination among locals and visitors</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has a <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_economy" title="Post-industrial economy">post-industrial economy</a> that is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector</a> (services), which generated 76.9% of output, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">secondary sector</a> (manufacturing, construction) at 22.2% and the <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary sector">primary sector</a> (agriculture, mining) at 0.8%.</p>
<p>The services sector is broadly diversified with financial services, wholesale and retail, information technology, commercial real estate, scientific research, and residential real estate each contributing at least 6% to the city's economy in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The single largest sub-sector remains industry, whose share of overall output has shrunk to 18.1% in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> The mix of industrial output has changed significantly since 2010 when the city announced that 140 highly-polluting, energy and water resource intensive enterprises would be relocated from the city in five years.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> The relocation of <a href="/wiki/Shougang_Corporation" title="Shougang Corporation">Capital Steel</a> to neighboring Hebei province had begun in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> In 2013, output of automobiles, aerospace products, semiconductors, pharmaceuticals, and food processing all increased.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the farmland around Beijing, vegetables and fruits have displaced grain as the primary crops under cultivation.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> In 2013, the tonnage of vegetable, edible fungus and fruit harvested was over three times that of grain.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> In 2013, overall acreage under cultivation shrank along with most categories of produce as more land was reforested for environmental reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_zones">Economic zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economic zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg/220px-Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg/330px-Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg/440px-Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg 2x" data-file-width="999" data-file-height="618" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_CBD_2008-8-23.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Beijing_CBD" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing CBD">Beijing CBD</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Beijing4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Central_Beijing4.jpg/220px-Central_Beijing4.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Central_Beijing4.jpg/330px-Central_Beijing4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Central_Beijing4.jpg/440px-Central_Beijing4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="804" data-file-height="465" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_Beijing4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Zhongguancun" title="Zhongguancun">Zhongguancun</a> is a technology hub in <a href="/wiki/Haidian_District" title="Haidian District">Haidian District</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_Financial_Street_(overlook).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg/220px-Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg/330px-Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg/440px-Beijing_Financial_Street_%28overlook%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="713" data-file-height="474" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_Financial_Street_(overlook).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Beijing_Financial_Street" title="Beijing Financial Street">Beijing Financial Street</a>, the financial center of Beijing</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_economic_and_technological_development_zones_in_Beijing" title="List of economic and technological development zones in Beijing">List of economic and technological development zones in Beijing</a></div>
<p>In 2006, the city government identified six high-end economic output zones around Beijing as the primary engines for local economic growth. In 2012, the six zones produced 43.3% of the city's GDP, up from 36.5% in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> The six zones are:</p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhongguancun" title="Zhongguancun">Zhongguancun</a>, China's silicon village in Haidian District northwest of the city, is home to both established and start-up tech companies. As of the second quarter of 2014, of the 9,895 companies registered in one of the six zones, 6,150 were based in Zhongguancun.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Financial_Street" title="Beijing Financial Street">Beijing Financial Street</a>, in Xicheng District on the west side of the city between Fuxingmen and Fuchengmen, is lined with headquarters of large state banks and insurance companies. The country's leading financial regulatory agencies including the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Bank_of_China" title="People's Bank of China">central bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Banking_Regulatory_Commission" title="China Banking Regulatory Commission">bank regulator</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Securities_Regulatory_Commission" title="China Securities Regulatory Commission">securities regulator</a>, and <a href="/wiki/State_Administration_of_Foreign_Exchange" title="State Administration of Foreign Exchange">foreign exchange authority</a> are all located in the neighborhood.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing_CBD" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing CBD">Beijing Central Business District (CBD)</a>, is actually located to the east of the city centre, near the embassies along the eastern Third Ring Road between Jianguomenwai and Chaoyangmenwai. The CBD is home to most of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Beijing" title="List of tallest buildings in Beijing">city's skyscraper office buildings</a>. Most of the city's foreign companies and professional service firms are based in the CBD.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Economic_and_Technological_Development_Area" title="Beijing Economic and Technological Development Area">Beijing Economic and Technological Development Area</a>, better known as <a href="/wiki/Yizhuang,_Beijing" title="Yizhuang, Beijing">Yizhuang</a>, is an industrial park the straddles the southern Fifth Ring Road in Daxing District. It has attracted pharmaceutical, information technology, and materials engineering companies.<sup id="cite_ref-social_economic_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-social_economic-111">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li>Beijing Airport Economic Zone was created in 1993 and surrounds the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing Capital International Airport</a> in Shunyi District northwest of the city. In addition to logistics, airline services, and trading firms, this zone is also home to Beijing's automobile assembly plants.</li>
<li>Beijing Olympic Center Zone surrounds the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Green" title="Olympic Green">Olympic Green</a> due north of the city centre and is developing into an entertainment, sports, tourism and business convention center.</li>
</ol>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shijingshan" class="mw-redirect" title="Shijingshan">Shijingshan</a>, on the western outskirts of the city, is a traditional heavy industrial base for steel-making.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> Chemical plants are concentrated in the far eastern suburbs.</p>
<p>Less legitimate enterprises also exist. Urban Beijing is known for being a center of <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">infringed</a> goods; anything from the latest designer clothing to DVDs can be found in markets all over the city, often marketed to expatriates and international visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Beijing" title="Demographics of Beijing">Demographics of Beijing</a></div>

<p>In 2013, Beijing had a total population of 21.148 million within the municipality, of which 18.251 million resided in urban districts or suburban townships and 2.897 million lived in rural villages.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> Within China, the city ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_China_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in China by population">second in urban population</a> after Shanghai and the <a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipalities_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipalities of China">third in municipal population</a> after Shanghai and Chongqing. Beijing also ranks among the most populous cities in the world, <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">a distinction the city has held for much of the past 800 years</a>, especially during the 15th to early 19th centuries when it was <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history" title="List of largest cities throughout history">the largest city in the world</a>.</p>
<p>About 13 million of the city's residents in 2013 had local <a href="/wiki/Hukou_system" title="Hukou system"><i>hukou</i> permits</a>, which entitles them to permanent residence in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> The remaining 8 million residents had <i>hukou</i> permits elsewhere and were not eligible to receive some social benefits provided by the Beijing municipal government.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The population increased in 2013 by 455,000 or about 7% from the previous year and continued a decade-long trend of rapid growth.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> The total population in 2004 was 14.213&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-2004pop_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004pop-114">[112]</a></sup> The population gains are driven largely by migration. The population's <a href="/wiki/Rate_of_natural_increase" title="Rate of natural increase">rate of natural increase</a> in 2013 was a mere 0.441%, based on a <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> of 8.93 and a <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> of 4.52.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">gender balance</a> was 51.6% males and 48.4% females.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Working age people account for nearly 80% of the population. Compared to 2004, residents age 0–14 as a proportion of the population dropped from 9.96% to 9.5% in 2013 and residents over the age of 65 declined from 11.12% to 9.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_98-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-98">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2004pop_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004pop-114">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2010 census, nearly 96% of Beijing's population are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-115">[113]</a></sup> Of the 800,000 ethnic minorities living in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Manchu_people" title="Manchu people">Manchu</a> (336,000), <a href="/wiki/Hui_people_in_Beijing" title="Hui people in Beijing">Hui</a> (249,000), <a href="/wiki/Korean_people_in_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean people in Beijing">Korean</a> (77,000), <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> (37,000) and <a href="/wiki/Tujia_people" title="Tujia people">Tujia</a> (24,000) constitute the five largest groups.<sup id="cite_ref-2010minorities_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010minorities-116">[114]</a></sup> In addition, there were 8,045 Hong Kong residents, 500 Macau residents, and 7,772 Taiwan residents along with 91,128 registered foreigners living in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-115">[113]</a></sup> A study by the Beijing Academy of Sciences estimates that in 2010 there were on average 200,000 foreigners living in Beijing on any given day including students, business travelers and tourists are not counted as registered residents.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2000 to 2010, the percentage of city residents with at least some college education nearly doubled from 16.8% to 31.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-115">[113]</a></sup> About 22.2% have some high school education and 31% had reached middle school.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_115-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg/170px-Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg/255px-Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg/340px-Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="573" data-file-height="727" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Beijing_observatory_14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Ancient_Observatory" title="Beijing Ancient Observatory">Old Beijing Observatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BeijingOperaProduction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/BeijingOperaProduction.jpg/220px-BeijingOperaProduction.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/BeijingOperaProduction.jpg/330px-BeijingOperaProduction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/BeijingOperaProduction.jpg/440px-BeijingOperaProduction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BeijingOperaProduction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A scene from a <a href="/wiki/Peking_opera" title="Peking opera">Peking opera</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cloisonneqing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cloisonneqing.jpg/220px-Cloisonneqing.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cloisonneqing.jpg/330px-Cloisonneqing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cloisonneqing.jpg/440px-Cloisonneqing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1165" data-file-height="939" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cloisonneqing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Chinese <a href="/wiki/Cloisonn%C3%A9" title="Cloisonné">cloisonné</a> dish from the Qing dynasty</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>People native to urban Beijing speak the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_dialect" title="Beijing dialect">Beijing dialect</a>, which belongs to the Mandarin subdivision of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_spoken_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese spoken language">spoken Chinese</a>. This speech is the basis for <i><a href="/wiki/Putonghua" class="mw-redirect" title="Putonghua">putonghua</a></i>, the standard spoken language used in mainland China and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, and one of the four official languages of <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. Rural areas of Beijing Municipality have <a href="/wiki/Jilu_Mandarin" title="Jilu Mandarin">their own dialects</a> akin to those of Hebei province, which surrounds Beijing Municipality.</p>
<p>Beijing or <a href="/wiki/Peking_opera" title="Peking opera">Peking opera</a> (<span lang="zh">京剧</span>, <i>Jīngjù</i>) is a traditional form of Chinese theatre well known throughout the nation. Commonly lauded as one of the highest achievements of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">Chinese culture</a>, Beijing opera is performed through a combination of song, spoken dialogue, and codified action sequences involving gestures, movement, fighting and acrobatics. Much of Beijing opera is carried out in an archaic stage dialect quite different from Modern Standard Chinese and from the modern Beijing dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Beijing_cuisine" title="Beijing cuisine">Beijing cuisine</a> is the local style of cooking. <a href="/wiki/Peking_Roast_Duck" class="mw-redirect" title="Peking Roast Duck">Peking Roast Duck</a> is perhaps the best known dish. <a href="/wiki/Fuling_Jiabing" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuling Jiabing">Fuling Jiabing</a>, a traditional Beijing snack food, is a pancake (<i>bing</i>) resembling a flat disk with a filling made from <i><a href="/wiki/Fu_Ling" class="mw-redirect" title="Fu Ling">fu ling</a></i>, a fungus used in traditional <a href="/wiki/Chinese_medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese medicine">Chinese medicine</a>. <a href="/wiki/Teahouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Teahouse">Teahouses</a> are common in Beijing.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cloisonn%C3%A9" title="Cloisonné">cloisonné</a> (or <i>Jingtailan</i>, literally "Blue of <a href="/wiki/Jingtai_Emperor" title="Jingtai Emperor">Jingtai</a>") metalworking technique and tradition is a Beijing art specialty, and is one of the most revered traditional crafts in China. Cloisonné making requires elaborate and complicated processes which include base-hammering, copper-strip inlay, soldering, enamel-filling, enamel-firing, surface polishing and gilding.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> Beijing's <a href="/wiki/Lacquerware" title="Lacquerware">lacquerware</a> is also well known for its sophisticated and intrinsic patterns and images carved into its surface, and the various decoration techniques of lacquer include "carved lacquer" and "engraved gold".</p>
<p>Younger residents of Beijing have become more attracted to the nightlife, which has flourished in recent decades, breaking prior cultural traditions that had practically restricted it to the upper class.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_interest">Places of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Places of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Major_National_Historical_and_Cultural_Sites_(Beijing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Major National Historical and Cultural Sites (Beijing)">Major National Historical and Cultural Sites (Beijing)</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Beijing_landmarks" title="List of Beijing landmarks">List of Beijing landmarks</a></div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>...the city remains an epicenter of tradition with the treasures of nearly 2,000 years as the imperial capital still on view—in the famed Forbidden City and in the city's lush pavilions and gardens...</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic</a><sup id="cite_ref-national_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-national-121">[119]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Qianmen_Street_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Qianmen_Street_1.jpg/220px-Qianmen_Street_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Qianmen_Street_1.jpg/330px-Qianmen_Street_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Qianmen_Street_1.jpg/440px-Qianmen_Street_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Qianmen_Street_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Qianmen_Avenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Qianmen Avenue">Qianmen Avenue</a>, a traditional commercial street in Beijing</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the historical heart of Beijing lies the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, the enormous palace compound that was the home of the emperors of the Ming and Qing dynasties;<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> the Forbidden City hosts the Palace Museum, which contains imperial collections of Chinese art. Surrounding the Forbidden City are several former imperial gardens, parks and scenic areas, notably <a href="/wiki/Beihai_Park" title="Beihai Park">Beihai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shichahai" title="Shichahai">Shichahai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhongnanhai" title="Zhongnanhai">Zhongnanhai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jingshan_Park" title="Jingshan Park">Jingshan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_(Beijing)" title="Zhongshan Park (Beijing)">Zhongshan</a>. These places, particularly Beihai Park, are described as masterpieces of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_garden" title="Chinese garden">Chinese gardening</a> art,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> and are popular tourist destinations with tremendous historical importance;<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> in the modern era, Zhongnanhai has also been the political heart of various Chinese governments and regimes and is now the headquarters of the Communist Party of China and the State Council. From Tiananmen Square, right across from the Forbidden City, there are several notable sites, such as the Tiananmen, <a href="/wiki/Qianmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Qianmen">Qianmen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Hall_of_the_People" title="Great Hall of the People">Great Hall of the People</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_China" title="National Museum of China">National Museum of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_People%27s_Heroes" title="Monument to the People's Heroes">Monument to the People's Heroes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Mausoleum of Mao Zedong">Mausoleum of Mao Zedong</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Summer_Palace" title="Summer Palace">Summer Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Old_Summer_Palace" title="Old Summer Palace">Old Summer Palace</a> both lie at the western part of the city; the former, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> contains a comprehensive collection of imperial gardens and palaces that served as the summer retreats for the Qing imperial family.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044,_Peking,_Himmelstempel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044%2C_Peking%2C_Himmelstempel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="469" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-009044,_Peking,_Himmelstempel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beijing's <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a> as photographed in the early 20th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the best known religious sites in the city is the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a> (<i>Tiantan</i>), located in southeastern Beijing, also a UNESCO World Heritage Site,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> where emperors of the Ming and Qing dynasties made visits for annual ceremonies of prayers to Heaven for good harvest. In the north of the city is the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Earth" title="Temple of Earth">Temple of Earth</a> (<i>Ditan</i>), while the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Sun" title="Temple of the Sun">Temple of the Sun</a> (<i>Ritan</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Moon_(China)" title="Temple of the Moon (China)">Temple of the Moon</a> (<i>Yuetan</i>) lie in the eastern and western urban areas respectively. Other well-known temple sites include the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Dongyue_Temple" title="Beijing Dongyue Temple">Dongyue Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzhe_Temple" title="Tanzhe Temple">Tanzhe Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miaoying_Temple" title="Miaoying Temple">Miaoying Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Cloud_Temple" title="White Cloud Temple">White Cloud Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yonghe_Temple" title="Yonghe Temple">Yonghe Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fayuan_Temple" title="Fayuan Temple">Fayuan Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wanshou_Temple" title="Wanshou Temple">Wanshou Temple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Bell_Temple" title="Big Bell Temple">Big Bell Temple</a>. The city also has its own <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Temple_of_Confucius" title="Beijing Temple of Confucius">Confucius Temple</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Guozijian_(Beijing)" title="Guozijian (Beijing)">Guozijian</a> or Imperial Academy. The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Immaculate_Conception_in_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception in Beijing">Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception</a>, built in 1605, is the oldest Catholic church in Beijing. The <a href="/wiki/Niujie_Mosque" title="Niujie Mosque">Niujie Mosque</a> is the oldest mosque in Beijing, with a history stretching back over a thousand years.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony,_Forbidden_City,_Beijing,_with_tourists_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg/220px-Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg/330px-Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg/440px-Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony%2C_Forbidden_City%2C_Beijing%2C_with_tourists_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5952" data-file-height="3917" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hall_of_Supreme_Harmony,_Forbidden_City,_Beijing,_with_tourists_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inside the Forbidden City</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beijing contains several well-preserved pagodas and stone pagodas, such as the towering <a href="/wiki/Pagoda_of_Tianning_Temple_(Beijing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pagoda of Tianning Temple (Beijing)">Pagoda of Tianning Temple</a>, which was built during the Liao Dynasty from 1100 to 1120, and the <a href="/wiki/Pagoda_of_Cishou_Temple" title="Pagoda of Cishou Temple">Pagoda of Cishou Temple</a>, which was built in 1576 during the Ming Dynasty. Historically noteworthy stone bridges include the 12th-century <a href="/wiki/Lugou_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugou Bridge">Lugou Bridge</a>, the 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Baliqiao" title="Baliqiao">Baliqiao</a> bridge, and the 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Jade_Belt_Bridge" title="Jade Belt Bridge">Jade Belt Bridge</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Ancient_Observatory" title="Beijing Ancient Observatory">Beijing Ancient Observatory</a> displays pre-telescopic spheres dating back to the Ming and Qing dynasties. The <a href="/wiki/Fragrant_Hills" title="Fragrant Hills">Fragrant Hills</a> (<i>Xiangshan</i>) is a popular scenic public park that consists of natural landscaped areas as well as traditional and cultural relics. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Botanical_Garden" title="Beijing Botanical Garden">Beijing Botanical Garden</a> exhibits over 6,000 species of plants, including a variety of trees, bushes and flowers, and an extensive <a href="/wiki/Peony" title="Peony">peony</a> garden. The <a href="/wiki/Taoranting_Park" title="Taoranting Park">Taoranting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Longtan_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Longtan Park">Longtan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Chaoyang_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Chaoyang Park">Chaoyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haidian_Park" title="Haidian Park">Haidian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milu_Yuan" title="Milu Yuan">Milu Yuan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purple_Bamboo_Park" title="Purple Bamboo Park">Zizhu Yuan</a> parks are some of the notable recreational parks in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Zoo" title="Beijing Zoo">Beijing Zoo</a> is a center of zoological research that also contains rare animals from various continents, including the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Giant_panda" title="Giant panda">giant panda</a>.</p>
<p>There are 144 museums and galleries (as of June 2008) in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-museum_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-129">[127]</a></sup> In addition to the Palace Museum in the Forbidden City and the National Museum of China, other major museums include the <a href="/wiki/National_Art_Museum_of_China" title="National Art Museum of China">National Art Museum of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_Museum" title="Capital Museum">Capital Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wanshou_Temple" title="Wanshou Temple">Beijing Art Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Military_Museum_of_the_Chinese_People%27s_Revolution" title="Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution">Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Geological_Museum_of_China" title="Geological Museum of China">Geological Museum of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Beijing Museum of Natural History">Beijing Museum of Natural History</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paleozoological_Museum_of_China" title="Paleozoological Museum of China">Paleozoological Museum of China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-museum_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-129">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Located at the outskirts of urban Beijing, but within its municipality are the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty_Tombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty Tombs">Thirteen Tombs of the Ming Dynasty</a>, the lavish and elaborate burial sites of thirteen Ming emperors, which have been designated as part of the UNESCO World Heritage Site <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Tombs_of_the_Ming_and_Qing_Dynasties" title="Imperial Tombs of the Ming and Qing Dynasties">Imperial Tombs of the Ming and Qing Dynasties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> The archaeological <a href="/wiki/Peking_Man" title="Peking Man">Peking Man</a> site at <a href="/wiki/Zhoukoudian" title="Zhoukoudian">Zhoukoudian</a> is another World Heritage Site within the municipality,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> containing a wealth of discoveries, among them one of the first specimens of <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> and an assemblage of bones of the gigantic <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">hyena</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pachycrocuta" title="Pachycrocuta">Pachycrocuta</a> brevirostris</i>. There are several sections of the UNESCO World Heritage Site <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> most notably <a href="/wiki/Badaling" title="Badaling">Badaling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinshanling" title="Jinshanling">Jinshanling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simatai" title="Simatai">Simatai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutianyu" title="Mutianyu">Mutianyu</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Beijing" title="List of tallest buildings in Beijing">List of tallest buildings in Beijing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Beijing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Beijing.jpg/220px-View_of_Beijing.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Beijing.jpg/330px-View_of_Beijing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/View_of_Beijing.jpg/440px-View_of_Beijing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Beijing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
City skyline looking east from the Financial Street</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three styles of architecture are predominant in urban Beijing. First, there is the traditional architecture of imperial China, perhaps best exemplified by the massive <a href="/wiki/Tian%27anmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Tian'anmen">Tian'anmen</a> (Gate of Heavenly Peace), which remains the People's Republic of China's trademark edifice, the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Ancestral_Temple" title="Imperial Ancestral Temple">Imperial Ancestral Temple</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a>. Next, there is what is sometimes referred to as the "Sino-Sov" style, with structures tending to be boxy and sometimes poorly constructed, which were built between the 1950s and the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> Finally, there are much more modern architectural forms, most noticeably in the area of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_CBD" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing CBD">Beijing CBD</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Financial_Street" title="Beijing Financial Street">Beijing Financial Street</a>.</p>
<p>In the early 21st century, Beijing has witnessed tremendous growth of new building constructions, exhibiting various modern styles from international designers. A mixture of both 1950s design and <a href="/wiki/Neofuturistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Neofuturistic">neofuturistic</a> style of architecture can be seen at the <a href="/wiki/798_Art_Zone" title="798 Art Zone">798 Art Zone</a>, which mixes the old with the new.</p>
<p>Beijing is famous for its <i><a href="/wiki/Siheyuan" title="Siheyuan">siheyuans</a></i>, a type of residence where a common courtyard is shared by the surrounding buildings. Among the more grand examples are the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Gong_Mansion" title="Prince Gong Mansion">Prince Gong Mansion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Former_Residence_of_Soong_Ching-ling_(Beijing)" title="Former Residence of Soong Ching-ling (Beijing)">Residence of Soong Ching-ling</a>. These courtyards are usually connected by alleys called <i><a href="/wiki/Hutong" title="Hutong">hutongs</a></i>. The <i>hutongs</i> are generally straight and run east to west so that doorways face north and south for good <a href="/wiki/Feng_Shui" class="mw-redirect" title="Feng Shui">Feng Shui</a>. They vary in width; some are so narrow only a few pedestrians can pass through at a time. Once ubiquitous in Beijing, <i>siheyuans</i> and <i>hutongs</i> are rapidly disappearing,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> as entire city blocks of <i>hutongs</i> are replaced by high-rise buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> Residents of the <i>hutongs</i> are entitled to live in the new buildings in apartments of at least the same size as their former residences. Many complain, however, that the traditional sense of community and street life of the <i>hutongs</i> cannot be replaced,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> and these properties are often government owned.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden">
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>

<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>
<p><br /></p>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Beijing</p>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C00000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Chinese_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese religion">Chinese religion</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">not religious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> (86.26%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (11.2%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (1.76%)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (0.78%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The religious heritage of Beijing is rich and diverse as <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> all have significant historical presence in the city. As the national capital, the city also hosts the <a href="/wiki/State_Administration_for_Religious_Affairs" title="State Administration for Religious Affairs">State Administration for Religious Affairs</a> and various state-sponsored institutions of the leading religions.<sup id="cite_ref-religion1_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-138">[136]</a></sup> In recent decades, foreign residents have brought other religious faiths to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-religion1_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion1-138">[136]</a></sup> According to Wang Zhiyun of the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences in 2010 there were 2.2 million Buddhists in the city, equal to 11.2% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> According to the Chinese General Social Survey of 2009, Christians constitute 0.78% of the city's population.<sup id="cite_ref-Wang2015_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wang2015-140">[138]</a></sup> According to a 2010 survey, Muslims constitute 1.76% of the population of Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-2010-Islam_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010-Islam-141">[139]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG/220px-The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG/330px-The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG/440px-The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3088" data-file-height="2056" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Temple_of_the_Town_Deity_in_Beijing1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of the temples of the City God of Beijing.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_folk_religion_and_Taoism">Chinese folk religion and Taoism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Chinese folk religion and Taoism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Beijing had many temples dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_gods_and_immortals" title="Chinese gods and immortals">folk religious deities</a>, many of which have been reconstructed or are being reconstructed in the 2000s and 2010s. Yearly sacrifices to the <a href="/wiki/Tian" title="Tian">God of Heaven</a> (祭天 <i>jìtiān</i>) at the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven" title="Temple of Heaven">Temple of Heaven</a> have been resumed by <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucian</a> groups in the 2010s.</p>
<p>There are temples dedicated to the worship of the Goddess (娘娘 <i>Niángniáng</i>) in the city, one of them near the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Olympic_Village" title="Beijing Olympic Village">Olympic Village</a>, and they revolve around a major cult centre at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Miaofeng" title="Mount Miaofeng">Mount Miaofeng</a>. There are also temples of the <a href="/wiki/Dragon_King" title="Dragon King">Dragon God</a> (龙神 <i>Lóngshén</i>) and temples of the <a href="/wiki/Chenghuangshen" class="mw-redirect" title="Chenghuangshen">City God</a> (城隍神 <i>Chénghuángshén</i>). Many of these temples are governed by the Beijing Taoist Association, such as the <a href="/wiki/Huode_Zhenjun_Temple" title="Huode Zhenjun Temple">Fire God Temple</a>.</p>
<p>The national <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taoist_Association" title="Chinese Taoist Association">Chinese Taoist Association</a> and Chinese Taoist College have their headquarters at the <a href="/wiki/White_Cloud_Temple" title="White Cloud Temple">White Cloud Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/Quanzhen_Taoism" class="mw-redirect" title="Quanzhen Taoism">Quanzhen Taoism</a>, which was founded in 741 and rebuilt numerous times. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Dongyue_Temple" title="Beijing Dongyue Temple">Beijing Dongyue Temple</a> outside Chaoyangmen is the largest temple of <a href="/wiki/Zhengyi_Taoism" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhengyi Taoism">Zhengyi Taoism</a> in the city. The Beijing Taoist Association has its headquarters at the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCzu_Temple" title="Lüzu Temple">Lüzu Temple</a> near Fuxingmen.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhism">Buddhism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Buddhism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg/220px-Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg/330px-Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg/440px-Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gfp-china-beijing-worshipping-at-lama-temple.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Yonghe_Temple" title="Yonghe Temple">Yonghe Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> was built in 1694.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_Association_of_China" title="Buddhist Association of China">Buddhist Association of China</a>, the state's supervisory organ overseeing all <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> institutions in mainland China, is headquartered in the <a href="/wiki/Guangji_Temple" title="Guangji Temple">Guangji Temple</a>, a temple founded over 800 years ago during the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty (1115–1234)</a> in what is now Fuchengmennei. The Beijing Buddhist Association along with the Buddhist Choir and Orchestra are based in the <a href="/wiki/Guanghua_Temple_(Beijing)" title="Guanghua Temple (Beijing)">Guanghua Temple</a>, which dates to the Yuan Dynasty over 700 years ago. The Buddhist Academy of China and its library are housed in the <a href="/wiki/Fayuan_Temple" title="Fayuan Temple">Fayuan Temple</a> near Caishikou. The Fayuan Temple, which dates to the Tang Dynasty 1300 years ago, is the oldest temple in urban Beijing. The Tongjiao Temple inside Dongzhimen is the city's only Buddhist nunnery.</p>
<p>The West Yellow Temple originally dates to the Liao Dynasty. In 1651, the temple was commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/Shunzhi_Emperor" title="Shunzhi Emperor">Qing Emperor Shunzhi</a> to host the visit of the <a href="/wiki/5th_Dalai_Lama" title="5th Dalai Lama">Fifth Dalai Lama</a> to Beijing. Since then, this temple has hosted the <a href="/wiki/13th_Dalai_Lama" title="13th Dalai Lama">13th Dalai Lama</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lobsang_Palden_Yeshe,_6th_Panchen_Lama" title="Lobsang Palden Yeshe, 6th Panchen Lama">Sixth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thubten_Choekyi_Nyima,_9th_Panchen_Lama" title="Thubten Choekyi Nyima, 9th Panchen Lama">Ninth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Choekyi_Gyaltsen,_10th_Panchen_Lama" title="Choekyi Gyaltsen, 10th Panchen Lama">Tenth</a> <a href="/wiki/Panchen_Lama" title="Panchen Lama">Panchen Lamas</a>. The largest Tibetan Buddhist Temple in Beijing is the Yonghe Temple, which was decreed by the <a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qing Emperor Qianlong</a> in 1744 to serve as the residence and research facility for his Buddhist preceptor of <a href="/wiki/Changkya_R%C3%B6lp%C3%A9_Dorj%C3%A9" title="Changkya Rölpé Dorjé">Rölpé Dorjé</a> the third <a href="/wiki/Changkya_Khutukhtu" title="Changkya Khutukhtu">Changkya</a> (or living Buddha of Inner Mongolia). The Yonghe Temple is so-named because it was the childhood residence of the <a href="/wiki/Yongzheng_Emperor" title="Yongzheng Emperor">Yongzheng Emperor</a>, and retains the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_glazed_roof_tile" title="Chinese glazed roof tile">glazed tiles</a> reserved for imperial palaces.</p>
<p>The Lingguang Temple of Badachu in the Western Hills also dates to the Tang Dynasty. The temple's Zhaoxian Pagoda was first built in 1071 during the Liao Dynasty to hold a tooth relic of the <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">Buddha</a>. The pagoda was destroyed during the Boxer Rebellion and the tooth was discovered from its foundation. A new pagoda was built in 1964. The six aforementioned temples: Guangji, Guanghua, Tongjiao, West Yellow, Yonghe and Lingguang have been designated <a href="/wiki/National_Key_Buddhist_Temples_in_Han_Chinese_Area" title="National Key Buddhist Temples in Han Chinese Area">National Key Buddhist Temples in Han Chinese Area</a>.</p>
<p>In addition, other notable temples in Beijing include the Tanzhe Temple (founded in the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin dynasty (265–420)">Jin dynasty (265–420)</a> is the oldest in the municipality), <a href="/wiki/Tianning_Temple_(Beijing)" title="Tianning Temple (Beijing)">Tianning Temple</a> (oldest pagoda in the city), <a href="/wiki/Miaoying_Temple" title="Miaoying Temple">Miaoying Temple</a> (famed for Yuan-era white dagoba), the Wanshou Temple (home to the Beijing Art Museum) and <a href="/wiki/Big_Bell_Temple" title="Big Bell Temple">Big Bell Temple</a>.</p>
<p><br /></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg/220px-Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg/330px-Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg/440px-Islamic_Association_of_China_20150613.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
