The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Association_of_China" title="Islamic Association of China">Islamic Association of China</a> near Niujie in Xicheng District.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Beijing has about 70 mosques recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Association_of_China" title="Islamic Association of China">Islamic Association of China</a>, whose headquarters are located next to the <a href="/wiki/Niujie_Mosque" title="Niujie Mosque">Niujie Mosque</a>, the oldest and most famous mosque in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> The Niujie Mosque was founded in 996 during the Liao Dynasty and is frequently visited by Muslim dignitaries. Other notable mosques in the old city include the <a href="/wiki/Dongsi_Mosque" title="Dongsi Mosque">Dongsi Mosque</a>, founded in 1346; the Huashi Mosque, founded in 1415; Nan Douya Mosque, near Chaoyangmen; Jinshifang Street Mosque, in Xicheng District; and the Dongzhimen Mosque.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> There are large mosques in outlying Muslim communities in Haidian, <a href="/wiki/Madian,_Beijing" title="Madian, Beijing">Madian</a>, Tongzhou, Changping, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Changying,_Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Changying, Beijing (page does not exist)">Changying</a>, Shijingshan and Miyun. The China Islamic Institute is located in the Niujie neighborhood in Xicheng District.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg/220px-Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg/330px-Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg/440px-Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1368" data-file-height="1824" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beijing_-_Xishiku_church_-_16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Saviour,_Beijing" title="Church of the Saviour, Beijing">Church of the Saviour</a>, also known as the Xishiku Church, founded in 1703.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholicism">Catholicism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Catholicism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 1289, <a href="/wiki/John_of_Montecorvino" title="John of Montecorvino">John of Montecorvino</a> came to Beijing as a <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> missionary with the order from the Pope. After meeting and receiving the support of <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> in 1293, he built the first Catholic church in Beijing in 1305. The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Patriotic_Catholic_Association" title="Chinese Patriotic Catholic Association">Chinese Patriotic Catholic Association</a> (CPCA), based in <a href="/wiki/Houhai" title="Houhai">Houhai</a> is the government oversight body for Catholics in mainland China. Notable Catholic churches in Beijing include:</p>
<ul>
<li>the Nantang or <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Immaculate_Conception,_Beijing" title="Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception, Beijing">Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception</a> also known as the Xuanwumen Church, which was founded in 1605 and whose current Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Li_Shan" title="Joseph Li Shan">Joseph Li Shan</a> is one of the few bishops in China to have the support of both the Vatican and the CPCA.</li>
<li>the Dongtang or <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_Church,_Beijing" title="St. Joseph's Church, Beijing">St. Joseph's Church</a>, better known as the Wangfujing Church, founded in 1653.</li>
<li>the Beitang or <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Saviour,_Beijing" title="Church of the Saviour, Beijing">Church of the Saviour</a>, also known as the Xishiku Church, founded in 1703.</li>
<li>the Xitang or <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel,_Beijing" title="Church of Our Lady of Mount Carmel, Beijing">Church of Our Lady of Mount Carmel</a> also known as the Xizhimen Church, founded in 1723.</li>
</ul>
<p>The National Seminary of Catholic Church in China is located in Daxing District.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">Protestantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Protestantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The earliest Protestant churches in Beijing were founded by <a href="/wiki/Protestant_missions_in_China_1807%E2%80%931953" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant missions in China 1807–1953">British and American missionaries</a> in the second half of the 19th century. Protestant missionaries also opened schools, universities and hospitals which have become important civic institutions. Most of Beijing's Protestant churches were destroyed during the <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxer Rebellion</a> and rebuilt. In 1958, the 64 Protestant churches in the city were reorganized into four and overseen by the state through the <a href="/wiki/Three-Self_Patriotic_Movement" title="Three-Self Patriotic Movement">Three-Self Patriotic Movement</a>. In the last 30 years, a number of new Protestant churches have opened in the city, including some by foreign expatriats.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gangwashichurch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Gangwashichurch.jpg/220px-Gangwashichurch.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Gangwashichurch.jpg/330px-Gangwashichurch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Gangwashichurch.jpg/440px-Gangwashichurch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gangwashichurch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gangwashi Church Church</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The London Missionary Society founded the Gangwashi Church in Xizhimen in 1863 and the Mishi Church in Dongdan in 1865. The Gangwashi Church was briefly renamed the <i>Xi Tang</i> or "West Church" in 1958. The Mishi Church which closed in 1958 but reopened in 1973, was for a time the only church in the city open to foreigners. In 1982, the congregation of the Mishi Church joined the Chongwenmen Church. The London Missionary Society Hospital, built near the Mishi Church, became part of the <a href="/wiki/Peking_Union_Medical_College_Hospital" title="Peking Union Medical College Hospital">Peking Union Medical College Hospital</a>. In 1907, the Church of England founded the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Saviour%27s_Cathedral_(Beijing)" title="Holy Saviour's Cathedral (Beijing)">Holy Saviour's Cathedral</a>, which no longer functions as a church but the architecture remains. Anglicans also founded Chongde Middle School (now No. 31 Middle School) and Duzhi Middle School (now Luxun Middle School).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zhushikou-Church.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Zhushikou-Church.jpg/220px-Zhushikou-Church.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Zhushikou-Church.jpg/330px-Zhushikou-Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Zhushikou-Church.jpg/440px-Zhushikou-Church.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3849" data-file-height="2577" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zhushikou-Church.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Zhushikou Church</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Methodist_Episcopal_Mission" title="American Methodist Episcopal Mission">American Methodist Episcopal Mission</a> founded eight churches in Beijing including the Zhushikou Church (renamed the <i>Nan Tang</i> or "South Church" in 1958), <a href="/wiki/Kuanjie_Protestant_Church" title="Kuanjie Protestant Church">Kuanjie Church</a> (renamed <i>Bei Tang</i> or "North Church" in 1958), the Chongwenmen Church and Huashi Church. The first three remain active houses of worship. The Huashi Church, like many other churches, was converted to other use and razed in 2004. The American Methodists also founded the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Tongren_Hospital" title="Beijing Tongren Hospital">Tongren Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Huiwen_Middle_School" title="Beijing Huiwen Middle School">Huiwen Middle School</a>, and Muchen Methodist Middle School for Girls (now No. 125 Middle School).<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg/220px-Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg/330px-Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg/440px-Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2924" data-file-height="2924" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haidian_Christian_Church_in_Beijing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Haidian_Christian_Church" title="Haidian Christian Church">Haidian Christian Church</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Board_of_Commissioners_for_Foreign_Missions" title="American Board of Commissioners for Foreign Missions">American Board of Commissioners for Foreign Missions</a>, representing the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" title="Congregational church">Congregational Church of America</a>, founded the Dengshikou Church (renamed the <i>Dong Tang</i> or "East Church" in 1958) and the <a href="/wiki/Haidian_Christian_Church" title="Haidian Christian Church">Haidian Church</a>. The Dengshikou Church was destroyed in 1966 during the Cultural Revolution. The Haidian Church now based in Zhongguancun was expanded in 2007. The Congregationalist missionaries also founded the Luhe Hospital, Yu Ying Boys' School (now No. 25 Middle School), Bridgeman Girls' School (now No. 166 Middle School), and Tongzhou Luhe Middle School.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_World_Mission" title="Presbyterian World Mission">American Presbyterian Mission in China</a> founded founded churches at Jiaodaokou and Gulou, which no longer exist. But the Chongci Girls' School (now No. 165 Middle School), Chongshi School (now No. 21 Middle School) continue in Jiaodaokou, and the <a href="/wiki/Deborah_Matilda_Douw" title="Deborah Matilda Douw">Douw Hospital for Women and Children</a> is now Beijing No. 6 Hospital. In addition, the Reverend Yasuzo Shimizu, a U.S.-educated Japanese Presbyterian missionary, founded the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Chen_Jing_Lun_High_School" title="Beijing Chen Jing Lun High School">Chongzhen Vocational and Grammar School for Girls</a> outside Chaoyangmen in 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> American Methodists, American Congressionalists and the London Missionary Society with the support of the American Presbyterian Mission China laid a foundation for the <a href="/wiki/Yenching_University" title="Yenching University">Yenching University</a>. The Yanjing Theological Seminary, formerly the theology department of the Yenching University, is now based in Qinghe. The <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> founded churches in Qianmen, Deshengmen, and Yuyou Hutong but none have survived as religious institutions.</p>
<p>In 2003, Three-Self Patriotic Movement opened the Chaoyang Church, the first new church opened under its jurisdiction since 1949. Newer Protestant churches that serve foreign expatriate community include the Beijing Baptist Church, Beijing International Christian Fellowship, Capital Community Church, Congregation of the Good Shepherd and the River of Grace Church.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Eastern Orthodox">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>There were a significant amount of Orthodox Christian in Beijing. Orthodox has come to Beijing along with <a href="/wiki/Albazinians" title="Albazinians">Russian prisoners</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sino-Russian_border_conflicts" title="Sino-Russian border conflicts">Albazino conflicts</a> in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> In 1956, Viktor, the bishop of Beijing returned to the Soviet Union, and the Soviet embassy took over the old cathedral and demolished it. In 2007, Russian embassy has rebuilt a new church in its garden to serve the Russian Orthodox Christian in Beijing.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_and_radio">Television and radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television and radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CCTV-new-building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/CCTV-new-building.jpg/220px-CCTV-new-building.jpg" width="220" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/CCTV-new-building.jpg/330px-CCTV-new-building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/CCTV-new-building.jpg/440px-CCTV-new-building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2370" data-file-height="2445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CCTV-new-building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/China_Central_Television_Headquarters_building" class="mw-redirect" title="China Central Television Headquarters building">China Central Television Headquarters building</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Television">Beijing Television</a> broadcasts on channels 1 through 10. Three radio stations feature programmes in English: <i>Hit FM</i> on FM 88.7, <i>Easy FM</i> by <a href="/wiki/China_Radio_International" title="China Radio International">China Radio International</a> on FM 91.5, and the newly launched <i>Radio 774</i> on AM 774. <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Radio_Stations" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing Radio Stations">Beijing Radio Stations</a> is the family of radio stations serving the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press">Press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The well-known <i><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Evening_News" title="Beijing Evening News">Beijing Evening News</a></i> (<i>Beijing Wanbao</i>, 北京晚报), covering news about Beijing in Chinese, is distributed every afternoon. Other newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Daily" title="Beijing Daily">Beijing Daily</a></i>, <i>The Beijing News</i> (<i>Xin Jing Bao</i>, 新京报), the <i>Beijing Star Daily</i>, the <i>Beijing Morning News</i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Youth_Daily" title="Beijing Youth Daily">Beijing Youth Daily</a></i> (<i>Beijing Qingnian Bao</i>), as well as English-language weeklies <i>Beijing Weekend</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Today" title="Beijing Today">Beijing Today</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People's Daily">People's Daily</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Times" title="Global Times">Global Times</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/China_Daily" title="China Daily">China Daily</a></i> (English) are published in Beijing as well.</p>
<p>Publications primarily aimed at international visitors and the expatriate community include the English-language periodicals <i>Time Out Beijing</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/City_Weekend" title="City Weekend">City Weekend</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Beijing_This_Month" title="Beijing This Month">Beijing This Month</a></i>, <i>Beijing Talk</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/That%27s_Beijing" title="That's Beijing">That's Beijing</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg/220px-2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg/330px-2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg/440px-2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="696" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_-_Fireworks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fireworks above <a href="/wiki/Venues_of_the_2008_Summer_Olympics" title="Venues of the 2008 Summer Olympics">Olympic venues</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2008 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Games</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG/220px-Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG/330px-Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG/440px-Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2240" data-file-height="1488" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martial_arts_-_Fragrant_Hills.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Taijiquan" class="mw-redirect" title="Taijiquan">Tai chi (Taijiquan)</a> practitioners at the <a href="/wiki/Fragrant_Hills" title="Fragrant Hills">Fragrant Hills</a> Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beijing has hosted numerous international and national sporting events, the most notable was the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympic</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Paralympics" title="2008 Summer Paralympics">Paralympic</a> Games. Other <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport</a> international events held in Beijing include the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Universiade" title="Universiade">Universiade</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1990_Asian_Games" title="1990 Asian Games">1990</a> <a href="/wiki/Asian_Games" title="Asian Games">Asian Games</a>. Single-sport international competitions include the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Marathon" title="Beijing Marathon">Beijing Marathon</a> (annually since 1981), <a href="/wiki/China_Open_(tennis)" title="China Open (tennis)">China Open of Tennis</a> (1993–97, annually since 2004), <a href="/wiki/ISU_Grand_Prix_of_Figure_Skating" title="ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating">ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating</a> <a href="/wiki/Cup_of_China" title="Cup of China">Cup of China</a> (<a href="/wiki/2003_Cup_of_China" title="2003 Cup of China">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_Cup_of_China" title="2004 Cup of China">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Cup_of_China" title="2005 Cup of China">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Cup_of_China" title="2008 Cup of China">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_Cup_of_China" title="2009 Cup of China">2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Cup_of_China" title="2010 Cup of China">2010</a>), <a href="/wiki/World_Professional_Billiards_and_Snooker_Association" title="World Professional Billiards and Snooker Association">WPBSA</a> <a href="/wiki/China_Open_(snooker)" title="China Open (snooker)">China Open for Snooker</a> (annually since 2005), <a href="/wiki/Union_Cycliste_Internationale" title="Union Cycliste Internationale">Union Cycliste Internationale</a> <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Beijing" title="Tour of Beijing">Tour of Beijing</a> (since <a href="/wiki/2011_Tour_of_Beijing" title="2011 Tour of Beijing">2011</a>), 1961 <a href="/wiki/World_Table_Tennis_Championships" title="World Table Tennis Championships">World Table Tennis Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/1987_IBF_World_Championships" title="1987 IBF World Championships">1987 IBF Badminton World Championships</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2004_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2004 AFC Asian Cup">2004 AFC Asian Cup</a> (football), and <a href="/wiki/2009_Barclays_Asia_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Barclays Asia Trophy">2009 Barclays Asia Trophy</a> (football). Beijing hosted the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015 IAAF World Championships in Athletics</a>.</p>
<p>Beijing's <a href="/wiki/LeSports_Center" title="LeSports Center">LeSports Center</a> will be one of the main venues for the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup">2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city hosted the second <a href="/wiki/National_Games_of_China" title="National Games of China">Chinese National Games</a> in 1914 and the first four <a href="/wiki/National_Games_of_China" title="National Games of China">National Games of China</a> in 1959, 1965, 1975, 1979, respectively, and co-hosted the 1993 National Games with <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>. Beijing also hosted the inaugural <a href="/wiki/National_Peasants%27_Games" title="National Peasants' Games">National Peasants' Games</a> in 1988 and the sixth National Minority Games in 1999.</p>
<p>In November 2013, Beijing made a <a href="/wiki/Beijing_bid_for_the_2022_Winter_Olympics" title="Beijing bid for the 2022 Winter Olympics">bid</a> to host the <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> On 31 July 2015, the International Olympic Committee awarded the 2022 Winter Olympics to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Major sporting venues in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_National_Stadium" title="Beijing National Stadium">National Stadium</a>, also known as the "Birds' Nest",<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beijing_National_Aquatics_Center" title="Beijing National Aquatics Center">National Aquatics Center</a>, also known as the "Water Cube", <a href="/wiki/Beijing_National_Indoor_Stadium" title="Beijing National Indoor Stadium">National Indoor Stadium</a>, all in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Green" title="Olympic Green">Olympic Green</a> to the north of city center; the <a href="/wiki/MasterCard_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard Center">MasterCard Center</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wukesong_Station" title="Wukesong Station">Wukesong</a> west of the city center; the <a href="/wiki/Workers_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Workers Stadium">Workers' Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Workers_Indoor_Arena" title="Workers Indoor Arena">Workers' Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sanlitun" title="Sanlitun">Sanlitun</a> just east of city center and the <a href="/wiki/Capital_Indoor_Stadium" title="Capital Indoor Stadium">Capital Arena</a> in Baishiqiao, northeast of the city center. In addition, many universities in the city have their own sport facilities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clubs">Clubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Clubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Olympians" title="Beijing Olympians">Beijing Olympians</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000%E2%80%93present)" title="American Basketball Association (2000–present)">American Basketball Association</a>, formerly a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Basketball_Association" title="Chinese Basketball Association">Chinese Basketball Association</a> team, kept their name and maintained a roster of primarily Chinese players after moving to <a href="/wiki/Maywood,_California" title="Maywood, California">Maywood, California</a> in 2005.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/China_Bandy_Federation" title="China Bandy Federation">China Bandy Federation</a> is based in Beijing, one of several cities in which the potential for <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a> development is explored.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Beijing is an important <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">transport hub</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">North China</a> with five <a href="/wiki/Ring_roads_of_Beijing" title="Ring roads of Beijing">ring roads</a>, nine expressways, eleven National Highways, nine conventional railways, and two high-speed railways converging on the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_high-speed_rail">Rail and high-speed rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Rail and high-speed rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing serves as a large rail hub in <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail transport in the People's Republic of China">China's railway network</a>. Ten conventional rail lines radiate from the city to: <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Shanghai_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Shanghai Railway">Shanghai (Jinghu Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou_Railway" title="Beijing–Guangzhou Railway">Guangzhou (Jingguang Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Kowloon_Railway" title="Beijing–Kowloon Railway">Kowloon (Jingjiu Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Harbin_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Harbin Railway">Harbin (Jingha Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Baotou_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Baotou Railway">Baotou (Jingbao Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Qinhuangdao_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Qinhuangdao Railway">Qinhuangdao (Jingqin Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Chengde_Railway" title="Beijing–Chengde Railway">Chengde (Jingcheng Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Tongliao_Railway" title="Beijing–Tongliao Railway">Tongliao, Inner Mongolia (Jingtong Line)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Yuanping_Railway" title="Beijing–Yuanping Railway">Yuanping, Shanxi (Jingyuan Line)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fengtai%E2%80%93Shacheng_Railway" title="Fengtai–Shacheng Railway">Shacheng, Hebei (Fengsha Line)</a>. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Datong%E2%80%93Qinhuangdao_Railway" title="Datong–Qinhuangdao Railway">Datong–Qinhuangdao Railway</a> passes through the municipality to the north of the city.</p>
<p>Beijing also has three <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> lines: the <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Tianjin_Intercity_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Tianjin Intercity Railway">Beijing-Tianjin Intercity Railway</a>, which opened in 2008; the <a href="/wiki/Beijing-Shanghai_High-Speed_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing-Shanghai High-Speed Railway">Beijing-Shanghai High-Speed Railway</a>, which opened in 2011; and the <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou%E2%80%93Shenzhen%E2%80%93Hong_Kong_High-Speed_Railway" title="Beijing–Guangzhou–Shenzhen–Hong Kong High-Speed Railway">Beijing–Guangzhou High-Speed Railway</a>, which opened in 2012.</p>
<p>The city's main railway stations are the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Railway_Station" title="Beijing Railway Station">Beijing Railway Station</a>, which opened in 1959; the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_West_Railway_Station" title="Beijing West Railway Station">Beijing West Railway Station</a>, which opened in 1996; and the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_South_Railway_Station" title="Beijing South Railway Station">Beijing South Railway Station</a>, which was rebuilt into the city's high-speed railway station in 2008. As of 1 July 2010, Beijing Railway Station had 173 trains arriving daily, Beijing West had 232 trains and Beijing South had 163. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_North_Railway_Station" title="Beijing North Railway Station">Beijing North Railway Station</a>, first built in 1909 and expanded in 2009, had 22 trains.</p>
<p>Smaller stations in the city including <a href="/wiki/Beijing_East_Railway_Station" title="Beijing East Railway Station">Beijing East Railway Station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qinghuayuan_Railway_Station" title="Qinghuayuan Railway Station">Qinghuayuan Railway Station</a> handle mainly commuter passenger traffic. The Fengtai Railway Station has been closed for renovation. In outlying suburbs and counties of Beijing, there are over 40 railway stations.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>From Beijing, <a href="/wiki/Passenger_rail_transport_in_China" title="Passenger rail transport in China">direct passenger train service</a> is available to most large cities in China. International train service is available to <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, Russia, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. Passenger trains in China are numbered according to their <a href="/wiki/Railroad_direction" class="mw-redirect" title="Railroad direction">direction</a> in relation to Beijing.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_expressways">Roads and expressways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Roads and expressways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Beijing" title="Expressways of Beijing">Expressways of Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highways_of_Beijing" title="China National Highways of Beijing">China National Highways of Beijing</a></div>
<p>Beijing is connected by road links to all parts of China as part of the National Trunk Road Network. Nine <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_China" title="Expressways of China">expressways of China</a> serve Beijing, as do eleven <a href="/wiki/China_National_Highway" class="mw-redirect" title="China National Highway">China National Highways</a>. Beijing's urban transport is dependent upon the five "<a href="/wiki/Ring_Roads_of_Beijing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring Roads of Beijing">ring roads</a>" that concentrically surround the city, with the <a href="/wiki/Forbidden_City" title="Forbidden City">Forbidden City</a> area marked as the geographical center for the ring roads. The ring roads appear more rectangular than ring-shaped. There is no official "1st Ring Road". The <a href="/wiki/2nd_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="2nd Ring Road">2nd Ring Road</a> is located in the inner city. Ring roads tend to resemble <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">expressways</a> progressively as they extend outwards, with the <a href="/wiki/5th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="5th Ring Road">5th</a> and <a href="/wiki/6th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="6th Ring Road">6th Ring Roads</a> being full-standard national expressways, linked to other roads only by interchanges. Expressways to other regions of China are generally accessible from the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Ring_Road_(Beijing)" title="3rd Ring Road (Beijing)">3rd Ring Road</a> outward. A final outer orbital, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=G95_Capital_Regional_Greater_Ring&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="G95 Capital Regional Greater Ring (page does not exist)">Capital Ring Expressway (G95)</a>, is being built and will extend into neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a>.</p>
<p>Within the urban core, city streets generally follow the checkerboard pattern of the ancient capital. Many of Beijing's boulevards and streets with "inner" and "outer" are still named in relation to gates in the city wall, though most gates no longer stand. Traffic jams are a major concern. Even outside of rush hour, several roads still remain clogged with traffic.</p>
<p>Beijing's urban design layout further exacerbates transportation problems.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> The authorities have introduced several bus lanes, which only public buses can use during rush hour. In the beginning of 2010, Beijing had 4 million registered automobiles.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> By the end of 2010, the government forecast 5 million. In 2010, new car registrations in Beijing averaged 15,500 per week.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Towards the end of 2010, the city government announced a series of drastic measures to tackle traffic jams, including limiting the number of new license plates issued to passenger cars to 20,000 a month and barring cars with non-Beijing plates from entering areas within the Fifth Ring Road during rush hour.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> More restrictive measures are also reserved during major events or heavily polluted weather.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing's primary airport is the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing Capital International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>: PEK) about 20 kilometres (12&#160;mi) northeast of the city center. The airport is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">second busiest airport in the world</a> after <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield-Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ACI_aero_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACI_aero-12">[12]</a></sup> After renovations for the 2008 Olympics, the airport now boasts three terminals, with Terminal 3 being one of the largest in the world. Most domestic and nearly all international flights arrive at and depart from Capital Airport. It is the main hub for <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a> and a hub for <a href="/wiki/China_Southern" class="mw-redirect" title="China Southern">China Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a>. The airport links Beijing with almost every other Chinese city with regular air passenger service.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Airport_Expressway_(Beijing)" title="Airport Expressway (Beijing)">Airport Expressway</a> links the airport to central Beijing; it is a roughly 40-minute drive from the city center during good traffic conditions. Prior to the 2008 Olympics, the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Airport_Expressway" title="2nd Airport Expressway">2nd Airport Expressway</a> was built to the airport, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> system, which now connects to the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">Beijing Subway</a>.</p>
<p>Other airports in the city include Liangxiang, <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Nanyuan_Airport" title="Beijing Nanyuan Airport">Nanyuan</a>, Xijiao, Shahe and Badaling. These airports are primarily for military use and are less well known to the public. Nanyuan serves as the hub for only one passenger airline. A second international airport, to be called <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport" title="Beijing Daxing International Airport">Beijing Daxing International Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> is currently being built in <a href="/wiki/Daxing_District" title="Daxing District">Daxing District</a>, and is expected to be open by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 1 January 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, tourists from 45 countries are permitted a 72-hour visa-free stay in Beijing. The 45 countries include Singapore, Japan, the United States, Canada, all EU and EEA countries (except Norway and Liechtenstein), Switzerland, Brazil, Argentina and Australia. The programme benefits transit and business travellers<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> with the 72 hours calculated starting from the moment visitors receive their transit stay permits rather than the time of their plane's arrival. Foreign visitors are not permitted to leave Beijing for other Chinese cities during the 72 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-Beijing_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beijing-164">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">Public transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Public transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Subway" title="Beijing Subway">Beijing Subway</a>, which began operating in 1969, now has 18 lines, 334 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Beijing_Subway_stations" title="List of Beijing Subway stations">stations</a>, and 554&#160;km (344&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">track</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">second longest subway system in the world</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metro_systems_by_annual_passenger_rides" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro systems by annual passenger rides">first in annual ridership</a> with 3.41 billion rides delivered in 2014. In 2013, with a flat fare of <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>2.00(0.31 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>) per ride with unlimited transfers on all lines except the <a href="/wiki/Airport_Express,_Beijing_Subway" title="Airport Express, Beijing Subway">Airport Express</a>, the subway was also the most affordable <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid transit in China">rapid transit in China</a>. The subway is undergoing rapid expansion and is expected to reach 30 lines, 450 stations, 1,050 kilometres (650&#160;mi) in length by 2020. When fully implemented, 95% residents inside the <a href="/wiki/4th_Ring_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="4th Ring Road">Fourth Ring Road</a> will be able walk to a station in 15 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Suburban_Railway" title="Beijing Suburban Railway">Beijing Suburban Railway</a> provides commuter rail service to outlying suburbs of the municipality.</p>
<p>On December 28, 2014, the Beijing Subway switched to a distance-based fare system from a fixed fare for all lines except the <a href="/wiki/Airport_Express,_Beijing_Subway" title="Airport Express, Beijing Subway">Airport Express</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-english.cri.cn_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-english.cri.cn-166">[164]</a></sup> Under the new system a trip under 6 <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a> will cost <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>3.00(0.49 USD), an additional <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>1.00 will be added for the next 6 kilometres (3.7 miles) and the next 10 kilometres (6.2 miles) until the distance for the trip reaches 32 kilometres (20 miles).<sup id="cite_ref-english.cri.cn_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-english.cri.cn-166">[164]</a></sup> For every 20 kilometres (12 miles) after the original 32 kilometres (20 miles) an additional <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>1.00 is added.<sup id="cite_ref-english.cri.cn_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-english.cri.cn-166">[164]</a></sup> For example, a 50 kilometres (31 miles) trip would cost <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a> 8.00.</p>
<p>There are nearly 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Bus" title="Beijing Bus">public bus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Tram_and_Trolleybus" title="Beijing Tram and Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> lines in the city, including four <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> lines. Standard bus fares are as low as ¥1.00 when purchased with the <i><a href="/wiki/Yikatong" title="Yikatong">Yikatong</a></i> metrocard.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Metered <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">taxi</a> in Beijing start at ¥13 for the first 3 kilometres (1.9&#160;mi), ¥2.3 <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">Renminbi</a> per additional 1 kilometre (0.62&#160;mi) and ¥1 per ride fuel surcharge, not counting idling fees which are ¥2.3 (¥4.6 during rush hours of 7–9 am and 5–7 pm) per 5 minutes of standing or running at speeds lower than 12 kilometres per hour (7.5&#160;mph) . Most taxis are <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra" title="Hyundai Elantra">Hyundai Elantras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Sonata" title="Hyundai Sonata">Hyundai Sonatas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citroën">Citroëns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta" title="Volkswagen Jetta">Volkswagen Jettas</a>. After 15 kilometres (9.3&#160;mi), the base fare increases by 50% (but is only applied to the portion <i>over</i> that distance). Different companies have special colors combinations painted on their vehicles. Usually registered taxis have yellowish brown as basic hue, with another color of Prussian blue, hunter green, white, umber, tyrian purple, rufous, or sea green. Between 11&#160;pm and 5&#160;am, there is also a 20% fee increase. Rides over 15&#160;km (9&#160;mi) and between 23:00 and 06:00 incur both charges, for a total increase of 80%. Tolls during trip should be covered by customers and the costs of trips beyond Beijing city limits should be negotiated with the driver. The cost of unregistered taxis is also subject to negotiation with the driver.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycles">Bicycles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Bicycles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beijing has long been well known for the number of bicycles on its streets. Although the rise of motor traffic has created a great deal of congestion and bicycle use has declined, bicycles are still an important form of local transportation. Large numbers of cyclists can be seen on most roads in the city, and most of the main roads have dedicated <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_lanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle lanes">bicycle lanes</a>. Beijing is relatively flat, which makes cycling convenient. The rise of <a href="/wiki/Electric_bicycles" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric bicycles">electric bicycles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_scooters" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric scooters">electric scooters</a>, which have similar speeds and use the same cycle lanes, may have brought about a revival in bicycle-speed two-wheeled transport. It is possible to cycle to most parts of the city. Because of the growing traffic congestion, the authorities have indicated more than once that they wish to encourage cycling, but it is not clear whether there is sufficient will to translate that into action on a significant scale.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_and_aerospace">Defense and aerospace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Defense and aerospace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg/220px-Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg/330px-Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg/440px-Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1478" data-file-height="941" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Korea_President_Park_China_Welcoming_Ceremony_20130627_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chinese President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a> and a military honor guard welcomes South Korean president <a href="/wiki/Park_Geun-hye" title="Park Geun-hye">Park Geun-hye</a> in June 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The command headquarters of China's military forces are based in Beijing. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Military_Commission_(China)" title="Central Military Commission (China)">Central Military Commission</a>, the political organ in charge of the military, is housed inside the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defense_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of National Defense of the People's Republic of China">Ministry of National Defense</a>, located next to the <a href="/wiki/Military_Museum_of_the_Chinese_People%27s_Revolution" title="Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution">Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution</a> in western Beijing. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Artillery_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Artillery Corps">Second Artillery Corps</a>, which controls the country's <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile" title="Intercontinental ballistic missile">strategic missile</a> and nuclear weapons, has its command in <a href="/wiki/Qinghe_Subdistrict,_Beijing" title="Qinghe Subdistrict, Beijing">Qinghe</a>, Haidian District. The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Military_Region" title="Beijing Military Region">Beijing Military Region</a>, one of seven nationally, is based further west in Gaojing. The Beijing Military Region oversees the Beijing Garrisons as well as the <a href="/wiki/27th_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="27th Army (People's Republic of China)">27th</a>, <a href="/wiki/38th_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="38th Army (People's Republic of China)">38th</a> and <a href="/wiki/65th_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="65th Army (People's Republic of China)">65th Armies</a>, which are based in Hebei.</p>
<p>Military institutions in Beijing also include academies and thinktanks such as the <a href="/wiki/PLA_National_Defence_University" title="PLA National Defence University">PLA National Defence University</a> and <a href="/wiki/PLA_Academy_of_Military_Science" title="PLA Academy of Military Science">Academy of Military Science</a>, military hospitals such as the <a href="/wiki/301_Military_Hospital" title="301 Military Hospital">301</a>, 307 and the Academy of Military Medical Sciences, and army-affiliated cultural entities such as the 1 August Film Studios and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Liberation_Army_Naval_Song_and_Dance_Troupe" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese People's Liberation Army Naval Song and Dance Troupe">PLA Song and Dance Troupe</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/China_National_Space_Administration" title="China National Space Administration">China National Space Administration</a>, which oversees country's <a href="/wiki/Chinese_space_program" title="Chinese space program">space program</a>, and several space-related state owned companies such as <a href="/wiki/China_Aerospace_Science_and_Technology_Corporation" title="China Aerospace Science and Technology Corporation">CASTC</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Aerospace_Science_and_Industry_Corporation" title="China Aerospace Science and Industry Corporation">CASIC</a> are all based in Beijing. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Aerospace_Command_and_Control_Center" title="Beijing Aerospace Command and Control Center">Beijing Aerospace Command and Control Center</a>, in Haidian District tracks the country's <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_program" title="Shenzhou program">manned</a> and unmanned flight and other space exploration initiatives.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_and_wildlife">Nature and wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Beijing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Nature and wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Beijing Municipality has 20 nature reserves that have a total area of 1,339.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (517.3&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> The mountains to the west and north of the city are home to a number of protected wildlife species including <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard_cat" title="Leopard cat">leopard cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolf">wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masked_palm_civet" title="Masked palm civet">masked palm civet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raccoon_dog" title="Raccoon dog">raccoon dog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hog_badger" title="Hog badger">hog badger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siberian_weasel" title="Siberian weasel">Siberian weasel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amur_hedgehog" title="Amur hedgehog">Amur hedgehog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_rat_snake" title="Mandarin rat snake">mandarin rat snake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> The Beijing Aquatic Wildlife Rescue and Conservation Center protects the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_giant_salamander" title="Chinese giant salamander">Chinese giant salamander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amur_stickleback" title="Amur stickleback">Amur stickleback</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_duck" title="Mandarin duck">mandarin duck</a> on the Huaijiu and Huaisha Rivers in <a href="/wiki/Huairou_District" title="Huairou District">Huairou District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Milu_Yuan" title="Milu Yuan">Beijing Milu Park</a> south of the city is home to one of the largest herds of <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A8re_David%27s_deer" title="Père David's deer">Père David's deer</a>, now extinct in the wild. The <a href="/wiki/Beijing_barbastelle" title="Beijing barbastelle">Beijing barbastelle</a>, a species of <a href="/wiki/Vesper_bat" title="Vesper bat">vesper bat</a> discovered in caves of <a href="/wiki/Fangshan_District" title="Fangshan District">Fangshan District</a> in 2001 and identified as a distinct species in 2007, is <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> to Beijing. The mountains of Fangshan are also habitat for the more common <a href="/wiki/Beijing_mouse-eared_bat" title="Beijing mouse-eared bat">Beijing mouse-eared bat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Large_myotis" title="Large myotis">large myotis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_horseshoe_bat" title="Greater horseshoe bat">greater horseshoe bat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rickett%27s_big-footed_bat" title="Rickett's big-footed bat">Rickett's big-footed bat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city flowers are the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_rose" title="Chinese rose">Chinese rose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chrysanthemum" title="Chrysanthemum">chrysanthemum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cityflowertree_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cityflowertree-174">[172]</a></sup> The city trees are the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_arborvitae" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese arborvitae">Chinese arborvitae</a>, an evergreen in the <a href="/wiki/Cypress" title="Cypress">cypress</a> <a href="/wiki/Cupressaceae" title="Cupressaceae">family</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pagoda_Tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Pagoda Tree">Pagoda Tree</a>, also called the Chinese scholar tree, a <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> tree of the <i><a href="/wiki/Fabaceae" title="Fabaceae">Fabaceae</a></i> family.<sup id="cite_ref-cityflowertree_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cityflowertree-174">[172]</a></sup> The oldest scholar tree in the city was planted in what is now <a href="/wiki/Beihai_Park" title="Beihai Park">Beihai Park</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a>, 1,300 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-gdp2013-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gdp2013_99-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">GDP-2013 are quarterly figures according to provisional data of China NBS (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.stats.gov.cn/">China NBS <b>National DATA</b> – quarterly figures (中文)</a> or <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://219.235.129.58/">China Statistical database – Quarterly Data (English)</a>); the comparable data of the world economies sources materials from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.imf.org/external/ns/cs.aspx?id=28">IMF – WEO – Database April 2014</a>; the annual average exchange rate CN￥6.1932 to USD 1 in 2013; for <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>, CNY 4.247 is equal to intl$.1 in 2013 according to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.imf.org/external/ns/cs.aspx?id=28">IMF – WEO – Database April 2014</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-gdppc2013-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-gdppc2013_100-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">GDP per capita figures are according to the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tjcn.org/plus/view.php?aid=26117"><i>2013 Statistical Communiqué of the provinces on National Economic and Social Development</i></a>, The annual average exchange rate is CNY 6.1932 per US dollar; <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) figures are according to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/weo/2013/01/weodata/index.aspx">April 2014 IMF data</a>. CNY 4.247 is equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Geary%E2%80%93Khamis_dollar" title="Geary–Khamis dollar">Intl. $</a> 1.</span></li>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="font-size:80%;">
<div><b>Note</b>: <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> is <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">claimed by the People's Republic of China</a> but administered by the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>). <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> are claimed as provincial-level divisions, but as listed on the constitutional documents and joint declarations their statuses are better to be interpreted as first-level divisions instead.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></div>

<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br />
<p><sup>a</sup><a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>. <sup>b</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>. <sup>c</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>. <sup>1</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>. <sup>2</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br />
<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br />
<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br />
<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. See <a href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China">Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br /></p>
All provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by province.</div>
</td>

<li><b><a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a></b>, <i><a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a></i>*</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>*</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;">
<div><b>*</b><a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a>.<br />
<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.<br />
<b>+</b> According to the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the Republic of China">Constitution of the Republic of China</a>, Nanjing is the official capital of the ROC, with Taipei as the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">seat of government</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>.</div>
